Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
The Imam's Exclusive Authority Over Captives
Imam's three options and exclusive authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options the Imam has for prisoners of war and explain why individual fighters cannot decide on their own.

Core Idea
Only the Imam decides the fate of captives; fighters must obey his judgment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq clarifies that the Imam alone may choose among killing, enslaving, or freeing prisoners as dhimmis. No individual soldier may kill a captive independently. We will examine the evidence from the Prophet’s practice and the rationale behind centralizing authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options for captives
List the three choices the Imam has: killing, enslaving, or freeing as dhimmis. Note which categories of prisoners are excluded.
Excluded: Arab polytheists and apostates.
2
Locate the proof for killing
The text cites the Prophet's action: 'because he (peace be upon him) killed.' This is a dalil naqli from the Sunnah.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad.
3
Understand the restriction to the Imam
The phrase 'it is restricted that the choice belongs to the Imam' means no fighter may kill without the Imam’s permission. The Imam may have a different assessment of maslahah.
The fighter who kills without necessity may be disciplined but not made liable for blood money.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
If a soldier kills a captive out of fear of harm, the Imam may discipline him but no financial compensation is required. This shows the failure of the act as a valid disposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المغرب عقره عقراً جرحه وعقر الناقة بالسيف ضرب قوائمها. والمواشي جمع ماشية وهي الإبل والبقر والغنم وقيد بالمواشي احترازاً عن النساء والصبيان التي يشق إخراجها فإنها تترك في أرض خربة حتى يموتوا جوعاً كيلا يعودوا حرباً علينا لأن النساء يقع بهن النسل، وأما الصبيان فإنهم يبلغون فيصيرون حرباً علينا ؛ كذا في فتاوى الولوالجي. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه أقوى من القتل المنهي عنه في قتل النساء والصبيان اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً لنهيه عن بيع الغنائم في دار الحرب والقسمة بيع معنى فتدخل تحته، ولأن الاستيلاء إثبات اليد الحافظة والناقلة والثاني منعدم لقدرتهم على الاستنقاذ ووجوده ظاهراً، والأصل عندنا أنه لا ملك قبل الإحراز بدار الإسلام فتحرم القسمة والبيع قبله ويشارك المدد العسكر قبله ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم قبل الاستيلاء عليهم، ولا يثبت نسب ولد أمة الأول في كلام المختصر (الخ قال في النهر : الظاهر أن مؤدى العبارتين واحد وذلك أن (ولا يصح قوله بغير شيء» أي بغير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ذمة وأن ردهم إلى دارهم هو إرسالهم إليها وهذا كما ترى مغاير لمطلق إطلاقهم بغير شيء فتدبره. ثم رأيته في إيضاح الإصلاح قال : المن أن يطلقهم مجاناً سواء كان الإطلاق بعد إسلامهم أو قبله أشير إلى ذلك في التعليل المذكور في الهداية يريد قوله : ولأنه بالأسر ثبت حق الاسترقاق فيه فلا يجوز إسقاطه بغير منفعة . ثم قال : وقد علم من نفي المن والفداء نفي ردهم إلى دارهم بطريق الدلالة فلا حاجة إلى ذكره اهـ . قوله : (ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم سيذكر عند قول المتن «لا السوقي» ما يخالفه
And in the Book of Siyar, Chapter of Spoils and their Division: Or he enslaves or leaves them free as dhimmis for us, and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor, and disabling. (And killing prisoners or enslaving them or leaving them free as dhimmis for us) means that the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he kills them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it cuts off the source of corruption; and if he wishes, he enslaves them because it repels their harm while providing abundant benefit for the Muslims; and if he wishes, he leaves them free as dhimmis for the Muslims as mentioned before, except for the Arab polytheists and apostates, for they are not enslaved nor do they become dhimmis, as we will explain if Allah wills. And he has no option for those who accept Islam among them except enslaving, because killing him or imposing jizyah upon him after his Islam is not permissible. It is restricted that the choice belongs to the Imam because no individual among the fighters may kill a prisoner by himself, because the decision is up to the Imam; he may see the benefit of the Muslims in enslaving him, so he may not intrude upon him. And accordingly, if he kills without necessity, such as if the killer fears the prisoner's harm, he (the Imam) may discipline him (the killer) if it occurs contrary to his intention, but he does not guarantee anything by his killing; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Qamus: al-asir is the captive, the bound, the imprisoned; plural asra, asara, and asra. His statement: (And it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor) because returning them strengthens them against the Muslims; ransoming them is aiding the disbelievers because he returns as a combatant against us, and repelling the evil of his war is better than rescuing the Muslim captive, because if he remains in their hands it is a trial for him not connected to us, and aiding by sending their captive to them is connected to us, so it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And they (the two disciples) permitted ransoming Muslim captives to rescue the Muslim, and the answer is as before. The prohibition of ransoming is general, including the old man from whom offspring is not expected. And from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is a narration of permissibility as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And the general includes the non-Muslim combatant, and taking a Muslim captive in exchange for him, and recovering from us with wealth we take from him. He said in al-Mughrib: Fadah from captivity: fida and fada means to rescue him with wealth; al-fidyah is the name of that wealth; al-mufada is between two people, one says fadahu when he releases him and takes his ransom. And from al-Mubarrad: al-mufada is that you give a man and take a man; al-fida is that you buy him; and it is said they are synonymous. End. And in the second there is a difference, according to the famous position of the school it is not permissible. And in al-Siyar al-Kabir: There is no problem with it if the Muslims have a need, using the captives of Badr as evidence. And if the captive accepted Islam in our hands, he is not ransomed for a Muslim captive in their hands, because it is of no benefit unless he is content with it, and he is safe concerning his Islam. As for granting favor (al-mann), he said in al-Qamus: Man 'alayhi mannan means he bestowed a favor and did a good deed for him. End. And the statements differ regarding its meaning here. In Fath al-Qadir: It is to release them to dar al-harb without anything. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Nihayah: It is to favor them by leaving them for free without executing the rulings upon them of killing or enslaving or leaving them as dhimmis for the Muslims. End. And the first is not correct in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) because it is the same as his saying 'and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb'; it is only forbidden because by capture the right of the gainers is established, so it is not permissible to nullify that without compensation like other spoils. And it is restricted to ransoming of disbelievers, because it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with those in dar al-harb using dirhams, dinars, and what does not contain fighting strength like clothes and other things. His statement: (And in the second there is a difference, i.e., purchasing him with wealth, and he called it 'second' in view of what is in al-Mubarrad's expression. His statement: Livestock difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned, and division of spoils in dirhams not for deposit and selling them before that. His statement: (And disabling livestock that are difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., it is forbidden to disable livestock because it is mutilation; he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the power of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like destroying buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place that the disbelievers do not find, to nullify their benefit. He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqarahu 'aqran means he wounded him; 'aqr al-naqa with the sword means hitting her legs. Al-mawashi is the plural of māshiyah, which are camels, cows, and sheep. It is restricted to livestock as a precaution against women and children whose removal is difficult; they are left in barren land until they die of hunger, so that they do not become combatants against us, because women give birth to offspring, and as for children, they grow up and become combatants against us. As in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And it was criticized in Fath al-Qadir by saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are forced to do so due to inability to carry; they leave them out of necessity, and this is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly said that they do that with women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he said: For this reason, our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in dar al-harb in their baggage, they remove the tail of the scorpion and fangs of the snake to cut harm from themselves, and they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in that, and we are commanded to oppose that. End. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Women from the people of Islam died in dar al-harb, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women. He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire. End. His statement: (And division of spoils in their land is not for deposit) i.e., it is forbidden to divide spoils in dar al-harb for other than deposit, because of his prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-harb, and division is a sale in meaning so it falls under it. And because possession is establishing a preserving and transferring hand, and the second is absent due to their ability to recover, though it exists apparently. And the principle with us is that there is no ownership before bringing to dar al-Islam, so division and selling before it are forbidden. And the reinforcements (al-madad) share with the army before that, even if from the people of war if they accepted Islam in their land before the seizure of them. And the lineage of a slave-girl's child is not established. The first in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) (etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently the import of the two expressions is one, and that is that (and it is not correct his saying 'without anything') i.e., without killing nor enslaving nor dhimma, and that returning them to their land is sending them to it, and this is as you see different from merely releasing them without anything, so ponder it. Then I saw in Idah al-Islah he said: al-Mann is to release them for free, whether the release is after their embracing Islam or before; that is indicated in the reasoning mentioned in al-Hidayah; he means his saying 'because by capture the right of enslaving is established, so it is not permissible to drop it without benefit.' Then he said: And it is known from the negation of mann and fida the negation of returning them to their land by way of implication, so there is no need to mention it. End. His statement: (And even if from the people of war if they accept Islam in their land) will be mentioned at his saying in the text 'not the market-goer' what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the chapter on spoils. It begins by explaining the Imam's three options for prisoners: killing, enslaving, or freeing as dhimmis. The proof is the Prophet's practice and the benefit of eliminating corruption or gaining utility. However, Arab polytheists and apostates cannot be enslaved or made dhimmis. The Imam alone decides; no soldier may kill a prisoner without his permission. If a soldier kills out of fear, the Imam may discipline him but no financial liability is incurred. The commentary then explains the prohibition of returning prisoners to dar al-harb, ransoming them, or granting them favor (mann). The reasoning is that these actions strengthen the enemy and violate the captors' rights. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits ransoming unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it to rescue Muslim captives, but the relied-upon position is prohibition except in cases of need as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. Ransoming with weapons is not allowed. The term 'mann' here means releasing without any compensation; it is forbidden because it annuls the captors' rights. Next, the text addresses livestock that cannot be taken: they may be slaughtered and burned to prevent enemy benefit. This is not mutilation but a legitimate destruction of property. Weapons and goods that cannot be transported should be burned or buried. Women and children who cannot be moved are left to die of hunger, as they would otherwise become enemies; this is not considered prohibited killing. Finally, spoils may not be divided in dar al-harb before being brought to dar al-Islam, because ownership is not established and division is akin to selling. Reinforcements who join before seizure share in the spoils. A cross-reference is given for a later discussion on the status of those who accept Islam in dar al-harb.

Key Terms
أسير (asīr): A captive prisoner of war, under the Imam's discretion.
خيار (khiyār): Option or choice; here the Imam's discretionary power over captives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if a fighter kills a captive without the Imam's permission out of fear of the captive's harm?
A) The fighter must pay blood money (diya).
B) The fighter is not liable for the killing but may be disciplined.
C) The fighter is executed for murder.
D) The killing is considered valid and no action is taken.

Key Takeaway
The Imam alone decides the fate of captives; individual fighters may not act independently.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Prohibitions: Returning, Ransoming, and Granting Favor
Prohibitions on returning, ransoming, and granting favor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits returning prisoners to dar al-harb, ransoming them, and granting them favor, and identify the intra-madhhab dispute on ransoming.

Core Idea
Returning, ransoming, or unconditionally freeing captives strengthens the enemy and nullifies Muslim rights.

This passage discusses three prohibited actions concerning prisoners: returning them to enemy territory, ransoming them (especially with money or prisoners), and granting them favor by releasing them without compensation. We will explore the rationale behind these prohibitions and the difference of opinion between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on ransoming.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
The text explicitly prohibits: (1) returning captives to dar al-harb, (2) ransoming them (fida), and (3) granting favor (mann). Write down each.
The prohibition applies to non-Muslim captives; Muslim captives have different rules.
2
Understand the rationale
Returning strengthens the enemy. Ransoming aids the enemy by giving them resources. Granting favor (unconditional release) nullifies the captors' right of ownership.
The captors have a right (haqq) to the captive after capture; releasing without compensation is like giving away spoils.
3
Examine the dispute on ransoming
Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits ransoming unconditionally. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it to rescue Muslim captives. The text cites the captives of Badr as evidence for permissibility, but the Hanafi response distinguishes that case.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is prohibition, but necessity may permit.
4
Apply the distinction between mann and return
Mann is unconditional release without any benefit to Muslims; returning sends them physically into enemy territory. Both are prohibited for similar reasons.
Some commentators conflate mann with return, but the text distinguishes them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عليه السلام قد قتل ولأن فيه حسم . مادة الفساد، وإن شاء استرقهم لأن فيه دفع شرهم مع وفور المنفعة لأهل الإسلام وإن شاء تركهم أحراراً ذمة للمسلمين لما بينا إلا مشركي العرب والمرتدين فإنهم لا يسترقون ولا يكونون ذمة على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى، وليس له فيمن أسلم منهم إلا الاسترقاق لأن قتله أو وضع الجزية عليه بعد إسلامه لا يجوز قيد بكون الخيار للإمام لأنه ليس لواحد من الغزاة أن يقتل أسيراً بنفسه لأن الرأي فيه إلى الإمام فقد يرى مصلحة المسلمين في استرقاقه فليس له أن يفتات عليه وعلى هذا فلو قتل بلا ملجئ بأن خاف القاتل شر الأسير كان له أن يعزره إذا وقع على خلاف مقصوده ولكن لا يضمن بقتله شيئاً؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي القاموس الأسير الأخيذ والمقيد والمسجون والجمع أسرى وأسارى وأسرى قوله : (وحرم ردهم إلى دار الحرب والفداء والمن) لأن في ردهم تقويتهم على المسلمين الفداء بهم معونة الكفرة لأنه يعود حرباً علينا ودفع شر حرابه خير من استخلاص الأسير المسلم لأنه إذا بقي في أيديهم كان ابتلاء في حقه غير مضاف إلينا، والإعانة بدفع أسيرهم إليهم مضاف إلينا فلا يجوز عند الإمام أبي حنيفة، وجوزا أن يفادى أسرى المسلمين تخليصاً للمسلم وجوابه ما مر . أطلق في منع الفداء فشمل الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يرجى له نسل. وعن محمد جوازه كما في الولوالجية، وشمل إطلاق الحربي وأخذ المسلم الأسير عوضاً عنه واستنقاذه منا بمال نأخذه منه . قال في المغرب : فداه من الأسر فداء وفدى استنقذه منه بمال، والفدية اسم ذلك المال، والمفاداة بين اثنين يقال فاداه إذا أطلقه وأخذ فديته. وعن المبرد: المفاداة أن تدفع رجلاً وتأخذ رجلاً والفداء أن تشتريه وقيل هما بمعنى .اهـ. وفي الثاني خلاف ففي المشهور من المذهب لا يجوز. وفي السير الكبير : لا بأس به إذا كان بالمسلمين حاجة استدلالاً بأسرى بدر، ولو كان أسلم الأسير في أيدينا لا يفادى بمسلم أسير في أيديهم لأنه لا يفيد إلا إذا طابت نفسه به وهو مأمون على إسلامه، وأما المن فقال في القاموس : من عليه مناً أنعم واصطنع عنده صنيعة اهـ. واختلفت العبارات في المراد به هنا ففي فتح القدير : هو أن يطلقهم إلى دار الحرب بغير شيء. وفي غاية البيان والنهاية : هو الإنعام عليهم بأن يتركهم مجاناً بدون إجراء الأحكام عليهم من القتل والاسترقاق أو تركهم ذمة للمسلمين .اهـ. ولا يصح الأول في كلام المختصر لأنه . هو عين قوله وحرم ردهم إلى دار الحرب وإنما حرم لأن بالأسر ثبت حق الغانمين فلا يجوز إبطال ذلك بغير عوض كسائر الأموال المغنومة. وقيد بفداء الكفار لأنه يجوز فداء أسرى المسلمين به الذين في دار الحرب بالدراهم والدنانير وما ليس فيه قوة للحرب كالثياب وغيرها قوله : (وفي الثاني (خلاف أي اشتراؤه بمال وسماه ثانياً نظراً إلى ما في عبارة المبرد. قوله : مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق وقسمة غنيمة في دراهم لا الإيداع وبيعها قبلها قوله : (وعقر مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق) أي وحرم عقر المواشي لأنه مثلة فيذبحها لأن ذبح الحيوان يجوز لغرض صحيح ولا غرض أصح من كسر شوكة الأعداء، ثم تحرق بالنار لتنقطع منفعته عن الكفار وصار كتخريب البنيان بخلاف التحريق قبل الذبح لأنه منهي عنه قال في المحيط : وأشار إلى أنه يحرق الأسلحة والأمتعة إذا تعذر نقلها وما لا يحترق منها يدفن في موضع لا يقف عليه الكفار إبطالاً للمنفعة عليهم. قال في المغرب عقره عقراً جرحه وعقر الناقة بالسيف ضرب قوائمها. والمواشي جمع ماشية وهي الإبل والبقر والغنم وقيد بالمواشي احترازاً عن النساء والصبيان التي يشق إخراجها فإنها تترك في أرض خربة حتى يموتوا جوعاً كيلا يعودوا حرباً علينا لأن النساء يقع بهن النسل، وأما الصبيان فإنهم يبلغون فيصيرون حرباً علينا ؛ كذا في فتاوى الولوالجي. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه أقوى من القتل المنهي عنه في قتل النساء والصبيان اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً وذكر بعده ولهذا قال علماؤنا : إذا وجد المسلمون حية أو عقرباً في دار الحرب في رحالهم ينزعون ذنب العقرب وأنياب الحية قطعاً للضرر عن أنفسهم ولا يقتلونها لأن فيه منفعة الكفار وقد أمرنا بضده .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : نساء من أهل الإسلام متن في دار الحرب فيطأ أهل الحرب النساء الأموات :قال يسعنا أن نحرقهن بالنار اهـ. قوله : ( وقسمة غنيمة في دارهم لا للإيداع أي حرم قسمة الغنائم في دار الحرب لغير إيداع لنهيه عن بيع الغنائم في دار الحرب والقسمة بيع معنى فتدخل تحته، ولأن الاستيلاء إثبات اليد الحافظة والناقلة والثاني منعدم لقدرتهم على الاستنقاذ ووجوده ظاهراً، والأصل عندنا أنه لا ملك قبل الإحراز بدار الإسلام فتحرم القسمة والبيع قبله ويشارك المدد العسكر قبله ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم قبل الاستيلاء عليهم، ولا يثبت نسب ولد أمة الأول في كلام المختصر (الخ قال في النهر : الظاهر أن مؤدى العبارتين واحد وذلك أن (ولا يصح قوله بغير شيء» أي بغير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ذمة وأن ردهم إلى دارهم هو إرسالهم إليها وهذا كما ترى مغاير لمطلق إطلاقهم بغير شيء فتدبره. ثم رأيته في إيضاح الإصلاح قال : المن أن يطلقهم مجاناً سواء كان الإطلاق بعد إسلامهم أو قبله أشير إلى ذلك في التعليل المذكور في الهداية يريد قوله : ولأنه بالأسر ثبت حق الاسترقاق فيه فلا يجوز إسقاطه بغير منفعة . ثم قال : وقد علم من نفي المن والفداء نفي ردهم إلى دارهم بطريق الدلالة فلا حاجة إلى ذكره اهـ . قوله : (ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم سيذكر عند قول المتن «لا السوقي» ما يخالفه
And in the Book of Siyar, Chapter of Spoils and their Division: Or he enslaves or leaves them free as dhimmis for us, and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor, and disabling. (And killing prisoners or enslaving them or leaving them free as dhimmis for us) means that the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he kills them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it cuts off the source of corruption; and if he wishes, he enslaves them because it repels their harm while providing abundant benefit for the Muslims; and if he wishes, he leaves them free as dhimmis for the Muslims as mentioned before, except for the Arab polytheists and apostates, for they are not enslaved nor do they become dhimmis, as we will explain if Allah wills. And he has no option for those who accept Islam among them except enslaving, because killing him or imposing jizyah upon him after his Islam is not permissible. It is restricted that the choice belongs to the Imam because no individual among the fighters may kill a prisoner by himself, because the decision is up to the Imam; he may see the benefit of the Muslims in enslaving him, so he may not intrude upon him. And accordingly, if he kills without necessity, such as if the killer fears the prisoner's harm, he (the Imam) may discipline him (the killer) if it occurs contrary to his intention, but he does not guarantee anything by his killing; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Qamus: al-asir is the captive, the bound, the imprisoned; plural asra, asara, and asra. His statement: (And it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor) because returning them strengthens them against the Muslims; ransoming them is aiding the disbelievers because he returns as a combatant against us, and repelling the evil of his war is better than rescuing the Muslim captive, because if he remains in their hands it is a trial for him not connected to us, and aiding by sending their captive to them is connected to us, so it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And they (the two disciples) permitted ransoming Muslim captives to rescue the Muslim, and the answer is as before. The prohibition of ransoming is general, including the old man from whom offspring is not expected. And from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is a narration of permissibility as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And the general includes the non-Muslim combatant, and taking a Muslim captive in exchange for him, and recovering from us with wealth we take from him. He said in al-Mughrib: Fadah from captivity: fida and fada means to rescue him with wealth; al-fidyah is the name of that wealth; al-mufada is between two people, one says fadahu when he releases him and takes his ransom. And from al-Mubarrad: al-mufada is that you give a man and take a man; al-fida is that you buy him; and it is said they are synonymous. End. And in the second there is a difference, according to the famous position of the school it is not permissible. And in al-Siyar al-Kabir: There is no problem with it if the Muslims have a need, using the captives of Badr as evidence. And if the captive accepted Islam in our hands, he is not ransomed for a Muslim captive in their hands, because it is of no benefit unless he is content with it, and he is safe concerning his Islam. As for granting favor (al-mann), he said in al-Qamus: Man 'alayhi mannan means he bestowed a favor and did a good deed for him. End. And the statements differ regarding its meaning here. In Fath al-Qadir: It is to release them to dar al-harb without anything. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Nihayah: It is to favor them by leaving them for free without executing the rulings upon them of killing or enslaving or leaving them as dhimmis for the Muslims. End. And the first is not correct in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) because it is the same as his saying 'and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb'; it is only forbidden because by capture the right of the gainers is established, so it is not permissible to nullify that without compensation like other spoils. And it is restricted to ransoming of disbelievers, because it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with those in dar al-harb using dirhams, dinars, and what does not contain fighting strength like clothes and other things. His statement: (And in the second there is a difference, i.e., purchasing him with wealth, and he called it 'second' in view of what is in al-Mubarrad's expression. His statement: Livestock difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned, and division of spoils in dirhams not for deposit and selling them before that. His statement: (And disabling livestock that are difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., it is forbidden to disable livestock because it is mutilation; he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the power of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like destroying buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place that the disbelievers do not find, to nullify their benefit. He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqarahu 'aqran means he wounded him; 'aqr al-naqa with the sword means hitting her legs. Al-mawashi is the plural of māshiyah, which are camels, cows, and sheep. It is restricted to livestock as a precaution against women and children whose removal is difficult; they are left in barren land until they die of hunger, so that they do not become combatants against us, because women give birth to offspring, and as for children, they grow up and become combatants against us. As in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And it was criticized in Fath al-Qadir by saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are forced to do so due to inability to carry; they leave them out of necessity, and this is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly said that they do that with women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he said: For this reason, our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in dar al-harb in their baggage, they remove the tail of the scorpion and fangs of the snake to cut harm from themselves, and they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in that, and we are commanded to oppose that. End. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Women from the people of Islam died in dar al-harb, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women. He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire. End. His statement: (And division of spoils in their land is not for deposit) i.e., it is forbidden to divide spoils in dar al-harb for other than deposit, because of his prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-harb, and division is a sale in meaning so it falls under it. And because possession is establishing a preserving and transferring hand, and the second is absent due to their ability to recover, though it exists apparently. And the principle with us is that there is no ownership before bringing to dar al-Islam, so division and selling before it are forbidden. And the reinforcements (al-madad) share with the army before that, even if from the people of war if they accepted Islam in their land before the seizure of them. And the lineage of a slave-girl's child is not established. The first in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) (etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently the import of the two expressions is one, and that is that (and it is not correct his saying 'without anything') i.e., without killing nor enslaving nor dhimma, and that returning them to their land is sending them to it, and this is as you see different from merely releasing them without anything, so ponder it. Then I saw in Idah al-Islah he said: al-Mann is to release them for free, whether the release is after their embracing Islam or before; that is indicated in the reasoning mentioned in al-Hidayah; he means his saying 'because by capture the right of enslaving is established, so it is not permissible to drop it without benefit.' Then he said: And it is known from the negation of mann and fida the negation of returning them to their land by way of implication, so there is no need to mention it. End. His statement: (And even if from the people of war if they accept Islam in their land) will be mentioned at his saying in the text 'not the market-goer' what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the chapter on spoils. It begins by explaining the Imam's three options for prisoners: killing, enslaving, or freeing as dhimmis. The proof is the Prophet's practice and the benefit of eliminating corruption or gaining utility. However, Arab polytheists and apostates cannot be enslaved or made dhimmis. The Imam alone decides; no soldier may kill a prisoner without his permission. If a soldier kills out of fear, the Imam may discipline him but no financial liability is incurred. The commentary then explains the prohibition of returning prisoners to dar al-harb, ransoming them, or granting them favor (mann). The reasoning is that these actions strengthen the enemy and violate the captors' rights. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits ransoming unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it to rescue Muslim captives, but the relied-upon position is prohibition except in cases of need as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. Ransoming with weapons is not allowed. The term 'mann' here means releasing without any compensation; it is forbidden because it annuls the captors' rights. Next, the text addresses livestock that cannot be taken: they may be slaughtered and burned to prevent enemy benefit. This is not mutilation but a legitimate destruction of property. Weapons and goods that cannot be transported should be burned or buried. Women and children who cannot be moved are left to die of hunger, as they would otherwise become enemies; this is not considered prohibited killing. Finally, spoils may not be divided in dar al-harb before being brought to dar al-Islam, because ownership is not established and division is akin to selling. Reinforcements who join before seizure share in the spoils. A cross-reference is given for a later discussion on the status of those who accept Islam in dar al-harb.

Key Terms
فداء (fidā'): Ransoming a prisoner by exchanging him for money or another person.
من (mann): Granting favor by releasing a prisoner without any compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'granting favor (mann)' prohibited?
A) It is a form of treason.
B) It nullifies the captors' right of ownership over the captive.
C) It makes the captive a dhimmi.
D) It violates international law.

Key Takeaway
Returning, ransoming, or granting favor to non-Muslim captives is prohibited because it harms Muslim interests and violates the captors' rights.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Disabling Livestock and Treatment of Women and Children
Ruling on disabling livestock and treatment of non-combatants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on disabling livestock that cannot be transported and the treatment of women and children left behind in dar al-harb.

Core Idea
Livestock that cannot be taken are slaughtered and burned to deny benefit to the enemy; women and children left behind may be left to die.

This passage addresses what to do with enemy property that cannot be carried away. Livestock are slaughtered and burned to prevent the enemy from using them. Women and children who cannot be moved are left to die of hunger, as they would otherwise become future combatants. This is a severe measure but based on necessity.

Guided Path
1
Define 'aqr' in this context
Aqr refers to disabling livestock by slaughtering them. The passage says it is not mutilation but a legitimate act to cut off enemy resources.
Aqr is normally prohibited (mutilation), but here it is allowed due to necessity.
2
Understand the procedure for livestock
If livestock cannot be taken out of enemy territory, they are slaughtered and then burned. This ensures no benefit reaches the enemy.
Burning before slaughter is prohibited (because it is torture), but after slaughter it is permissible.
3
Know the rule for weapons and goods
Weapons and goods that cannot be transported are burned or buried to deny their use.
This is analogous to destroying buildings.
4
Treat women and children left behind
If women and children cannot be taken, they are left in barren land to die of hunger. This is because women bear future soldiers and children grow into soldiers.
This is a drastic measure only when removal is impossible; some scholars criticized it as harsher than killing.
5
Note the exception for snakes/scorpions
If Muslims find harmful creatures in their camp, they disable them (remove fangs/stingers) but do not kill, because killing would benefit the enemy (dead animals could be used).
This illustrates the principle of denying enemy benefit.

إلى دار الحرب بغير شيء. وفي غاية البيان والنهاية : هو الإنعام عليهم بأن يتركهم مجاناً بدون إجراء الأحكام عليهم من القتل والاسترقاق أو تركهم ذمة للمسلمين .اهـ. ولا يصح الأول في كلام المختصر لأنه . هو والدنانير وما ليس فيه قوة للحرب كالثياب وغيرها قوله : (وفي الثاني (خلاف أي اشتراؤه بمال وسماه ثانياً نظراً إلى ما في عبارة المبرد. قوله : مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق وقسمة غنيمة في دراهم لا الإيداع وبيعها قبلها قوله : (وعقر مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق) أي وحرم عقر المواشي لأنه مثلة فيذبحها لأن ذبح الحيوان يجوز لغرض صحيح ولا غرض أصح من كسر شوكة الأعداء، ثم تحرق بالنار لتنقطع منفعته عن الكفار وصار كتخريب البنيان بخلاف التحريق قبل الذبح لأنه منهي عنه قال في المحيط : وأشار إلى أنه يحرق الأسلحة والأمتعة إذا تعذر نقلها وما لا يحترق منها يدفن في موضع لا يقف عليه الكفار إبطالاً للمنفعة عليهم. قال في المغرب عقره عقراً جرحه وعقر الناقة بالسيف ضرب قوائمها. والمواشي جمع ماشية وهي الإبل والبقر والغنم وقيد بالمواشي احترازاً عن النساء والصبيان التي يشق إخراجها فإنها تترك في أرض خربة حتى يموتوا جوعاً كيلا يعودوا حرباً علينا لأن النساء يقع بهن النسل، وأما الصبيان فإنهم يبلغون فيصيرون حرباً علينا ؛ كذا في فتاوى الولوالجي. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه أقوى من القتل المنهي عنه في قتل النساء والصبيان اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً وذكر بعده ولهذا قال علماؤنا : إذا وجد المسلمون حية أو عقرباً في دار الحرب في رحالهم ينزعون ذنب العقرب وأنياب الحية قطعاً للضرر عن أنفسهم ولا يقتلونها لأن فيه منفعة الكفار وقد أمرنا بضده .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : نساء من أهل الإسلام متن في دار الحرب فيطأ أهل الحرب النساء الأموات :قال يسعنا أن نحرقهن بالنار اهـ. قوله : ( وقسمة غنيمة في دارهم لا للإيداع أي حرم قسمة الغنائم في دار الحرب لغير إيداع لنهيه عن بيع الغنائم في دار الحرب والقسمة بيع معنى فتدخل تحته، ولأن الاستيلاء إثبات اليد الحافظة والناقلة والثاني منعدم لقدرتهم على الاستنقاذ ووجوده ظاهراً، والأصل عندنا أنه لا ملك قبل الإحراز بدار الإسلام فتحرم القسمة والبيع قبله ويشارك المدد العسكر قبله ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم قبل الاستيلاء عليهم، ولا يثبت نسب ولد أمة الأول في كلام المختصر (الخ قال في النهر : الظاهر أن مؤدى العبارتين واحد وذلك أن (ولا يصح قوله بغير شيء» أي بغير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ذمة وأن ردهم إلى دارهم هو إرسالهم إليها وهذا كما ترى مغاير لمطلق إطلاقهم بغير شيء فتدبره. ثم رأيته في إيضاح الإصلاح قال : المن أن يطلقهم مجاناً سواء كان الإطلاق بعد إسلامهم أو قبله أشير إلى ذلك في التعليل المذكور في الهداية يريد قوله : ولأنه بالأسر ثبت حق الاسترقاق فيه فلا يجوز إسقاطه بغير منفعة . ثم قال : وقد علم من نفي المن والفداء نفي ردهم إلى دارهم بطريق الدلالة فلا حاجة إلى ذكره اهـ . قوله : (ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم سيذكر عند قول المتن «لا السوقي» ما يخالفه
And in the Book of Siyar, Chapter of Spoils and their Division: Or he enslaves or leaves them free as dhimmis for us, and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor, and disabling. (And killing prisoners or enslaving them or leaving them free as dhimmis for us) means that the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he kills them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it cuts off the source of corruption; and if he wishes, he enslaves them because it repels their harm while providing abundant benefit for the Muslims; and if he wishes, he leaves them free as dhimmis for the Muslims as mentioned before, except for the Arab polytheists and apostates, for they are not enslaved nor do they become dhimmis, as we will explain if Allah wills. And he has no option for those who accept Islam among them except enslaving, because killing him or imposing jizyah upon him after his Islam is not permissible. It is restricted that the choice belongs to the Imam because no individual among the fighters may kill a prisoner by himself, because the decision is up to the Imam; he may see the benefit of the Muslims in enslaving him, so he may not intrude upon him. And accordingly, if he kills without necessity, such as if the killer fears the prisoner's harm, he (the Imam) may discipline him (the killer) if it occurs contrary to his intention, but he does not guarantee anything by his killing; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Qamus: al-asir is the captive, the bound, the imprisoned; plural asra, asara, and asra. His statement: (And it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor) because returning them strengthens them against the Muslims; ransoming them is aiding the disbelievers because he returns as a combatant against us, and repelling the evil of his war is better than rescuing the Muslim captive, because if he remains in their hands it is a trial for him not connected to us, and aiding by sending their captive to them is connected to us, so it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And they (the two disciples) permitted ransoming Muslim captives to rescue the Muslim, and the answer is as before. The prohibition of ransoming is general, including the old man from whom offspring is not expected. And from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is a narration of permissibility as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And the general includes the non-Muslim combatant, and taking a Muslim captive in exchange for him, and recovering from us with wealth we take from him. He said in al-Mughrib: Fadah from captivity: fida and fada means to rescue him with wealth; al-fidyah is the name of that wealth; al-mufada is between two people, one says fadahu when he releases him and takes his ransom. And from al-Mubarrad: al-mufada is that you give a man and take a man; al-fida is that you buy him; and it is said they are synonymous. End. And in the second there is a difference, according to the famous position of the school it is not permissible. And in al-Siyar al-Kabir: There is no problem with it if the Muslims have a need, using the captives of Badr as evidence. And if the captive accepted Islam in our hands, he is not ransomed for a Muslim captive in their hands, because it is of no benefit unless he is content with it, and he is safe concerning his Islam. As for granting favor (al-mann), he said in al-Qamus: Man 'alayhi mannan means he bestowed a favor and did a good deed for him. End. And the statements differ regarding its meaning here. In Fath al-Qadir: It is to release them to dar al-harb without anything. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Nihayah: It is to favor them by leaving them for free without executing the rulings upon them of killing or enslaving or leaving them as dhimmis for the Muslims. End. And the first is not correct in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) because it is the same as his saying 'and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb'; it is only forbidden because by capture the right of the gainers is established, so it is not permissible to nullify that without compensation like other spoils. And it is restricted to ransoming of disbelievers, because it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with those in dar al-harb using dirhams, dinars, and what does not contain fighting strength like clothes and other things. His statement: (And in the second there is a difference, i.e., purchasing him with wealth, and he called it 'second' in view of what is in al-Mubarrad's expression. His statement: Livestock difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned, and division of spoils in dirhams not for deposit and selling them before that. His statement: (And disabling livestock that are difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., it is forbidden to disable livestock because it is mutilation; he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the power of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like destroying buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place that the disbelievers do not find, to nullify their benefit. He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqarahu 'aqran means he wounded him; 'aqr al-naqa with the sword means hitting her legs. Al-mawashi is the plural of māshiyah, which are camels, cows, and sheep. It is restricted to livestock as a precaution against women and children whose removal is difficult; they are left in barren land until they die of hunger, so that they do not become combatants against us, because women give birth to offspring, and as for children, they grow up and become combatants against us. As in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And it was criticized in Fath al-Qadir by saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are forced to do so due to inability to carry; they leave them out of necessity, and this is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly said that they do that with women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he said: For this reason, our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in dar al-harb in their baggage, they remove the tail of the scorpion and fangs of the snake to cut harm from themselves, and they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in that, and we are commanded to oppose that. End. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Women from the people of Islam died in dar al-harb, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women. He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire. End. His statement: (And division of spoils in their land is not for deposit) i.e., it is forbidden to divide spoils in dar al-harb for other than deposit, because of his prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-harb, and division is a sale in meaning so it falls under it. And because possession is establishing a preserving and transferring hand, and the second is absent due to their ability to recover, though it exists apparently. And the principle with us is that there is no ownership before bringing to dar al-Islam, so division and selling before it are forbidden. And the reinforcements (al-madad) share with the army before that, even if from the people of war if they accepted Islam in their land before the seizure of them. And the lineage of a slave-girl's child is not established. The first in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) (etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently the import of the two expressions is one, and that is that (and it is not correct his saying 'without anything') i.e., without killing nor enslaving nor dhimma, and that returning them to their land is sending them to it, and this is as you see different from merely releasing them without anything, so ponder it. Then I saw in Idah al-Islah he said: al-Mann is to release them for free, whether the release is after their embracing Islam or before; that is indicated in the reasoning mentioned in al-Hidayah; he means his saying 'because by capture the right of enslaving is established, so it is not permissible to drop it without benefit.' Then he said: And it is known from the negation of mann and fida the negation of returning them to their land by way of implication, so there is no need to mention it. End. His statement: (And even if from the people of war if they accept Islam in their land) will be mentioned at his saying in the text 'not the market-goer' what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the chapter on spoils. It begins by explaining the Imam's three options for prisoners: killing, enslaving, or freeing as dhimmis. The proof is the Prophet's practice and the benefit of eliminating corruption or gaining utility. However, Arab polytheists and apostates cannot be enslaved or made dhimmis. The Imam alone decides; no soldier may kill a prisoner without his permission. If a soldier kills out of fear, the Imam may discipline him but no financial liability is incurred. The commentary then explains the prohibition of returning prisoners to dar al-harb, ransoming them, or granting them favor (mann). The reasoning is that these actions strengthen the enemy and violate the captors' rights. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits ransoming unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it to rescue Muslim captives, but the relied-upon position is prohibition except in cases of need as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. Ransoming with weapons is not allowed. The term 'mann' here means releasing without any compensation; it is forbidden because it annuls the captors' rights. Next, the text addresses livestock that cannot be taken: they may be slaughtered and burned to prevent enemy benefit. This is not mutilation but a legitimate destruction of property. Weapons and goods that cannot be transported should be burned or buried. Women and children who cannot be moved are left to die of hunger, as they would otherwise become enemies; this is not considered prohibited killing. Finally, spoils may not be divided in dar al-harb before being brought to dar al-Islam, because ownership is not established and division is akin to selling. Reinforcements who join before seizure share in the spoils. A cross-reference is given for a later discussion on the status of those who accept Islam in dar al-harb.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): Disabling or wounding animals, specifically by slaughtering and burning livestock that cannot be transported.
مثلة (muthla): Mutilation; prohibited in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on burning weapons and goods that cannot be transported?
A) Prohibited because it is wasteful.
B) Permissible to prevent enemy use.
C) Obligatory to return them to the enemy.
D) Only allowed if the Imam permits.

Key Takeaway
Destroying enemy property that cannot be taken is permissible to deny benefit, but must avoid mutilation.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
7 min
Prohibition of Dividing Spoils in Dar al-Harb
Prohibition of dividing spoils before ihtiyaz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school forbids dividing spoils in dar al-harb before bringing them to dar al-Islam.

Core Idea
Spoils cannot be divided in enemy territory because ownership is not established until safely in Muslim territory.

This passage explains that spoils may not be divided or sold in dar al-harb. Division is akin to selling, which is prohibited. The reason is that full ownership (tamleek) does not occur until the spoils are brought to dar al-Islam (ihraz). This rule also affects the share of reinforcements who join before seizure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
The text explicitly forbids dividing spoils in dar al-harb except for the purpose of deposit. Division is equated to sale.
Deposit (ida') means entrusting to a trustworthy person for safekeeping, not distribution.
2
Understand the evidence
The evidence is a prophetic prohibition against selling spoils in dar al-harb. Since division is like a sale, it falls under the same ruling.
The text cites a hadith but does not quote it verbatim: 'prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-harb.'
3
Grasp the legal principle
The principle (asl) is that there is no ownership (milk) before ihtiyaz (taking possession in Islamic territory). Therefore, any transaction transferring ownership is invalid.
This is a key difference from some other schools that may allow division earlier.
4
Apply to reinforcements (al-madad)
Reinforcements who join the army before the seizure of spoils share in the spoils even if they did not participate, because ownership is not yet established.
This also applies if the reinforcements were originally from dar al-harb but accepted Islam before seizure.

اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً التتارخانية : نساء من أهل الإسلام متن في دار الحرب فيطأ أهل الحرب النساء الأموات :قال يسعنا أن نحرقهن بالنار اهـ. قوله : ( وقسمة غنيمة في دارهم لا للإيداع أي حرم قسمة الغنائم في دار الحرب لغير إيداع لنهيه عن بيع الغنائم في دار الحرب والقسمة بيع معنى فتدخل تحته، ولأن الاستيلاء إثبات اليد الحافظة والناقلة والثاني منعدم لقدرتهم على الاستنقاذ ووجوده ظاهراً، والأصل عندنا أنه لا ملك قبل الإحراز بدار الإسلام فتحرم القسمة والبيع قبله ويشارك المدد العسكر قبله ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم قبل الاستيلاء عليهم، ولا يثبت نسب ولد أمة الأول في كلام المختصر (الخ قال في النهر : الظاهر أن مؤدى العبارتين واحد وذلك أن (ولا يصح قوله بغير شيء» أي بغير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ذمة وأن ردهم إلى دارهم هو إرسالهم إليها وهذا كما ترى مغاير لمطلق إطلاقهم بغير شيء فتدبره. ثم رأيته في إيضاح الإصلاح قال : المن أن يطلقهم مجاناً سواء كان الإطلاق بعد إسلامهم أو قبله أشير إلى ذلك في التعليل المذكور في الهداية يريد قوله : ولأنه بالأسر ثبت حق الاسترقاق فيه فلا يجوز إسقاطه بغير منفعة . ثم قال : وقد علم من نفي المن والفداء نفي ردهم إلى دارهم بطريق الدلالة فلا حاجة إلى ذكره اهـ . قوله : (ولو من أهل الحرب إذا أسلموا بدارهم سيذكر عند قول المتن «لا السوقي» ما يخالفه
And in the Book of Siyar, Chapter of Spoils and their Division: Or he enslaves or leaves them free as dhimmis for us, and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor, and disabling. (And killing prisoners or enslaving them or leaving them free as dhimmis for us) means that the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he kills them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it cuts off the source of corruption; and if he wishes, he enslaves them because it repels their harm while providing abundant benefit for the Muslims; and if he wishes, he leaves them free as dhimmis for the Muslims as mentioned before, except for the Arab polytheists and apostates, for they are not enslaved nor do they become dhimmis, as we will explain if Allah wills. And he has no option for those who accept Islam among them except enslaving, because killing him or imposing jizyah upon him after his Islam is not permissible. It is restricted that the choice belongs to the Imam because no individual among the fighters may kill a prisoner by himself, because the decision is up to the Imam; he may see the benefit of the Muslims in enslaving him, so he may not intrude upon him. And accordingly, if he kills without necessity, such as if the killer fears the prisoner's harm, he (the Imam) may discipline him (the killer) if it occurs contrary to his intention, but he does not guarantee anything by his killing; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Qamus: al-asir is the captive, the bound, the imprisoned; plural asra, asara, and asra. His statement: (And it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and granting favor) because returning them strengthens them against the Muslims; ransoming them is aiding the disbelievers because he returns as a combatant against us, and repelling the evil of his war is better than rescuing the Muslim captive, because if he remains in their hands it is a trial for him not connected to us, and aiding by sending their captive to them is connected to us, so it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And they (the two disciples) permitted ransoming Muslim captives to rescue the Muslim, and the answer is as before. The prohibition of ransoming is general, including the old man from whom offspring is not expected. And from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is a narration of permissibility as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And the general includes the non-Muslim combatant, and taking a Muslim captive in exchange for him, and recovering from us with wealth we take from him. He said in al-Mughrib: Fadah from captivity: fida and fada means to rescue him with wealth; al-fidyah is the name of that wealth; al-mufada is between two people, one says fadahu when he releases him and takes his ransom. And from al-Mubarrad: al-mufada is that you give a man and take a man; al-fida is that you buy him; and it is said they are synonymous. End. And in the second there is a difference, according to the famous position of the school it is not permissible. And in al-Siyar al-Kabir: There is no problem with it if the Muslims have a need, using the captives of Badr as evidence. And if the captive accepted Islam in our hands, he is not ransomed for a Muslim captive in their hands, because it is of no benefit unless he is content with it, and he is safe concerning his Islam. As for granting favor (al-mann), he said in al-Qamus: Man 'alayhi mannan means he bestowed a favor and did a good deed for him. End. And the statements differ regarding its meaning here. In Fath al-Qadir: It is to release them to dar al-harb without anything. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Nihayah: It is to favor them by leaving them for free without executing the rulings upon them of killing or enslaving or leaving them as dhimmis for the Muslims. End. And the first is not correct in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) because it is the same as his saying 'and it is forbidden to return them to dar al-harb'; it is only forbidden because by capture the right of the gainers is established, so it is not permissible to nullify that without compensation like other spoils. And it is restricted to ransoming of disbelievers, because it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with those in dar al-harb using dirhams, dinars, and what does not contain fighting strength like clothes and other things. His statement: (And in the second there is a difference, i.e., purchasing him with wealth, and he called it 'second' in view of what is in al-Mubarrad's expression. His statement: Livestock difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned, and division of spoils in dirhams not for deposit and selling them before that. His statement: (And disabling livestock that are difficult to take out, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., it is forbidden to disable livestock because it is mutilation; he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the power of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like destroying buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place that the disbelievers do not find, to nullify their benefit. He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqarahu 'aqran means he wounded him; 'aqr al-naqa with the sword means hitting her legs. Al-mawashi is the plural of māshiyah, which are camels, cows, and sheep. It is restricted to livestock as a precaution against women and children whose removal is difficult; they are left in barren land until they die of hunger, so that they do not become combatants against us, because women give birth to offspring, and as for children, they grow up and become combatants against us. As in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And it was criticized in Fath al-Qadir by saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are forced to do so due to inability to carry; they leave them out of necessity, and this is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly said that they do that with women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he said: For this reason, our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in dar al-harb in their baggage, they remove the tail of the scorpion and fangs of the snake to cut harm from themselves, and they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in that, and we are commanded to oppose that. End. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Women from the people of Islam died in dar al-harb, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women. He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire. End. His statement: (And division of spoils in their land is not for deposit) i.e., it is forbidden to divide spoils in dar al-harb for other than deposit, because of his prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-harb, and division is a sale in meaning so it falls under it. And because possession is establishing a preserving and transferring hand, and the second is absent due to their ability to recover, though it exists apparently. And the principle with us is that there is no ownership before bringing to dar al-Islam, so division and selling before it are forbidden. And the reinforcements (al-madad) share with the army before that, even if from the people of war if they accepted Islam in their land before the seizure of them. And the lineage of a slave-girl's child is not established. The first in the statement of the author (al-Mukhtasar) (etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently the import of the two expressions is one, and that is that (and it is not correct his saying 'without anything') i.e., without killing nor enslaving nor dhimma, and that returning them to their land is sending them to it, and this is as you see different from merely releasing them without anything, so ponder it. Then I saw in Idah al-Islah he said: al-Mann is to release them for free, whether the release is after their embracing Islam or before; that is indicated in the reasoning mentioned in al-Hidayah; he means his saying 'because by capture the right of enslaving is established, so it is not permissible to drop it without benefit.' Then he said: And it is known from the negation of mann and fida the negation of returning them to their land by way of implication, so there is no need to mention it. End. His statement: (And even if from the people of war if they accept Islam in their land) will be mentioned at his saying in the text 'not the market-goer' what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the chapter on spoils. It begins by explaining the Imam's three options for prisoners: killing, enslaving, or freeing as dhimmis. The proof is the Prophet's practice and the benefit of eliminating corruption or gaining utility. However, Arab polytheists and apostates cannot be enslaved or made dhimmis. The Imam alone decides; no soldier may kill a prisoner without his permission. If a soldier kills out of fear, the Imam may discipline him but no financial liability is incurred. The commentary then explains the prohibition of returning prisoners to dar al-harb, ransoming them, or granting them favor (mann). The reasoning is that these actions strengthen the enemy and violate the captors' rights. Imam Abu Hanifa prohibits ransoming unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it to rescue Muslim captives, but the relied-upon position is prohibition except in cases of need as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. Ransoming with weapons is not allowed. The term 'mann' here means releasing without any compensation; it is forbidden because it annuls the captors' rights. Next, the text addresses livestock that cannot be taken: they may be slaughtered and burned to prevent enemy benefit. This is not mutilation but a legitimate destruction of property. Weapons and goods that cannot be transported should be burned or buried. Women and children who cannot be moved are left to die of hunger, as they would otherwise become enemies; this is not considered prohibited killing. Finally, spoils may not be divided in dar al-harb before being brought to dar al-Islam, because ownership is not established and division is akin to selling. Reinforcements who join before seizure share in the spoils. A cross-reference is given for a later discussion on the status of those who accept Islam in dar al-harb.

Key Terms
إيداع (īdā‘): Deposit; entrusting property to a trustworthy person for safekeeping.
إحراز (iḥrāz): The act of bringing spoils into safe Muslim territory, which establishes full ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on selling spoils in dar al-harb?
A) Permissible if all soldiers agree.
B) Prohibited because it is like dividing spoils.
C) Permissible only for food items.
D) Prohibited only for weapons.

Key Takeaway
Spoils must not be divided or sold in enemy territory; full ownership is established only after reaching dar al-Islam.

Disposal of Enemy Livestock: Slaughter and Burn, Not Hamstring
Commentary on the ruling for livestock and property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of enemy livestock and explain the distinction between hamstringing (haram) and slaughtering (mubah) based on the principles of muthla and denial of benefit.

Core Idea
Hamstringing livestock is mutilation (muthla) and haram; slaughtering and burning are permissible to deny the enemy benefit.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author clarifies the ruling for enemy livestock that cannot be transported. The text explicitly prohibits hamstringing (ʿaqr) because it is mutilation (muthla), but permits slaughtering and burning to prevent the enemy from using the animals. We will examine the evidence and the analogical reasoning behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
Locate the ruling on hamstringing (ʿaqr). The text states it is prohibited. Understand why: it is a form of mutilation (muthla), which is categorically forbidden.
The term ʿaqr means to wound an animal's legs so it cannot move, akin to crippling.
2
Identify the permissible alternatives
The text says livestock should be slaughtered and then burned. Slaughtering is permissible for a valid purpose, and burning after slaughter prevents the enemy from benefiting.
Burning before slaughter is prohibited because it is wasteful and cruel.
3
Locate the proofs
The prohibition of hamstringing is based on the general prohibition of muthla (mutilation) established in hadith. The permissibility of slaughtering and burning is based on qiyas (analogy) to demolishing buildings, which is allowed to deny benefit to the enemy.
The text explicitly compares burning to demolition of buildings.
4
Analyze the qiyas
Break down the analogy: asl (original case) = demolishing buildings (mubah); farʿ (new case) = slaughtering and burning livestock; illa (effective cause) = denial of benefit to the enemy; hukm (ruling) = mubah.
The illa is clear: both actions prevent the enemy from using the property.
5
Note the exception for weapons and equipment
The text adds that weapons and other items that cannot be transported should be burned; non-combustible items should be buried. This follows the same principle of nullifying enemy benefit.
This expansion shows the consistency of the rule across different types of property.

Source Text

كتاب السير/ باب الغنائم وقسمتها
مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق وقسمة غنيمة في دارهم لا للإيداع وبيعها قبلها
ولا يفادون بالسلاح ؛ كذا في غاية البيان وظاهر الولوالجية أنه يجوز مفاداة أسرى المسلمين بالسلاح والكراع اتفاقاً قوله : (وعقر مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق) أي وحرم عقر المواشي لأنه مثلة فيذبحها لأن ذبح الحيوان يجوز لغرض صحيح ولا غرض أصح من كسر شوكة الأعداء، ثم تحرق بالنار لتنقطع منفعته عن الكفار وصار كتخريب البنيان بخلاف التحريق قبل الذبح لأنه منهي عنه قال في المحيط : وأشار إلى أنه يحرق الأسلحة والأمتعة إذا تعذر نقلها وما لا يحترق منها يدفن في موضع لا يقف عليه الكفار إبطالاً للمنفعة عليهم. قال في المغرب عقره عقراً جرحه وعقر الناقة بالسيف ضرب قوائمها. والمواشي جمع ماشية وهي الإبل والبقر والغنم وقيد بالمواشي احترازاً عن النساء والصبيان التي يشق إخراجها فإنها تترك في أرض خربة حتى يموتوا جوعاً كيلا يعودوا حرباً علينا لأن النساء يقع بهن النسل، وأما الصبيان فإنهم يبلغون فيصيرون حرباً علينا ؛ كذا في فتاوى الولوالجي. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه أقوى من القتل المنهي عنه في قتل النساء والصبيان اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً وذكر بعده ولهذا قال علماؤنا : إذا وجد المسلمون حية أو عقرباً في دار الحرب في رحالهم ينزعون ذنب العقرب وأنياب الحية قطعاً للضرر عن أنفسهم ولا يقتلونها لأن فيه منفعة الكفار وقد أمرنا بضده .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : نساء من أهل الإسلام متن في دار الحرب فيطأ أهل الحرب النساء الأموات :قال يسعنا أن نحرقهن بالنار اهـ.
The Book of Siyar / Chapter of Spoils and Their Division. Livestock whose extraction is difficult, so they are slaughtered and burned. Division of spoils in their land is not for deposit, nor selling them before that. And they are not to be ransomed with weapons. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And the apparent of al-Walwalji is that it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with weapons and horses by agreement. His statement: (And the hamstringing of livestock whose extraction is difficult, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., the hamstringing of livestock is prohibited because it is mutilation. So he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the strength of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like demolishing buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: 'And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn of them is buried in a place where the disbelievers will not come across it, to nullify the benefit for them.' He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqara ya'qiru 'aqran means he wounded him, and 'aqr of the she-camel with the sword is striking her legs.' Al-Mawashi is the plural of mashi, which are camels, cows, and sheep. The restriction to livestock is to exclude women and children whose extraction is difficult, for they are left in a ruined land until they die of hunger so that they do not become hostile to us again, because women give birth, and as for children, they will grow up and become hostile to us. Thus in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And he criticized it in Fath al-Qadir, saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are compelled to that due to lack of carrying capacity, so they are left out of necessity. And it is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly stated that this is done to women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he mentioned: 'For this reason our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in the land of war in their baggage, they remove the scorpion's stinger and the snake's fangs to cut off harm from themselves, but they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in them, and we have been commanded to oppose that.' End quote. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'Women from the people of Islam who die in the land of war, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women: He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire.' End quote.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining the ruling on disposing of enemy property that cannot be transported. The author begins by clarifying the matn: livestock that are difficult to extract should be slaughtered and burned, not hamstrung, because hamstringing is a form of mutilation (muthla) which is haram. Slaughtering is permissible for a valid purpose, and breaking the enemy's strength is the most valid purpose. Burning after slaughter is allowed to prevent the enemy from benefiting, analogous to demolishing buildings. However, burning before slaughter is prohibited. The commentary then addresses the treatment of women and children: if they cannot be transported, they are left in a ruined land to die from hunger, but they are not directly killed. This is based on the principle that direct killing of women and children is prohibited unless necessary. The author defends al-Walwalji's position against Fath al-Qadir's criticism. An interesting subsidiary ruling is given about snakes and scorpions: Muslims should only remove their harmful parts, not kill them, because the animals' bodies would benefit the enemy. Finally, a fatwa on dead Muslim women: if enemy soldiers violate their corpses, it is permissible to burn the bodies to prevent this desecration.

Key Terms
عقر (ʿaqr): Hamstringing or wounding an animal's legs so it cannot move; here specifically meaning to disable livestock.
مواش (mawāshī): Livestock, including camels, cows, and sheep.
مثلة (muthla): Mutilation of a living or dead body, including hamstringing, cutting off limbs, etc., which is prohibited in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hamstringing (ʿaqr) of livestock prohibited according to this passage?
A) Because it causes unnecessary suffering to animals
B) Because it is a form of mutilation (مثلة) which is haram
C) Because the animals might be used by the enemy
D) Because it is less effective than slaughtering

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering and burning enemy livestock to deny benefit is permissible; hamstringing is prohibited as mutilation.
