Treating Enemy Women and Children in Dar al-Harb: Indirect Cessation
Commentary on the ruling for women and children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on leaving enemy women and children in dar al-harb when extraction is impossible, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Walwalji and Fath al-Qadir.

Core Idea
Women and children are not directly killed; if removal is impossible, they may be left to die indirectly to prevent future hostility.

This passage addresses a difficult scenario in war: what to do with enemy women and children who cannot be transported. The Hanafi school permits leaving them in a ruined land to die of hunger, but this ruling has been criticized by some later scholars. We will examine the reasoning, the controversy, and the resolution provided by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The text says women and children whose extraction is difficult are left in a ruined land until they die of hunger. Note: they are not directly killed.
The ruling is conditional on impossibility of transport.
2
Understand the effective cause (illa)
The reason given: women give birth to future warriors; children grow up to become warriors. Thus, leaving them prevents future hostility.
This is a form of indirect prevention, not direct killing.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Fath al-Qadir criticized this ruling as 'stronger than the prohibited killing.' The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends al-Walwalji by clarifying that it is only when removal is impossible.
The criticism was based on a misunderstanding of the condition.
4
Examine the supporting analogy
The text brings an analogy: Muslims find a snake or scorpion in their camp in dar al-harb. They remove its harmful parts but do not kill it, because the dead body would benefit the enemy. Similarly, women and children are not killed outright.
This illustrates the principle of indirect harm prevention.
5
Apply to a subsidiary ruling
The text ends with a fatwa: if Muslim women die in dar al-harb and enemy soldiers violate their corpses, it is permissible to burn the bodies to prevent desecration.
This follows the same theme of preventing benefit to the enemy (here, sexual gratification).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب الغنائم وقسمتها
مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق وقسمة غنيمة في دارهم لا للإيداع وبيعها قبلها
ولا يفادون بالسلاح ؛ كذا في غاية البيان وظاهر الولوالجية أنه يجوز مفاداة أسرى المسلمين بالسلاح والكراع اتفاقاً قوله : (وعقر مواش شق إخراجها فتذبح وتحرق) أي وحرم عقر المواشي لأنه مثلة فيذبحها لأن ذبح الحيوان يجوز لغرض صحيح ولا غرض أصح من كسر شوكة الأعداء، ثم تحرق بالنار لتنقطع منفعته عن الكفار وصار كتخريب البنيان بخلاف التحريق قبل الذبح لأنه منهي عنه قال في المحيط : وأشار إلى أنه يحرق الأسلحة والأمتعة إذا تعذر نقلها وما لا يحترق منها يدفن في موضع لا يقف عليه الكفار إبطالاً للمنفعة عليهم. قال في المغرب عقره عقراً جرحه وعقر الناقة بالسيف ضرب قوائمها. والمواشي جمع ماشية وهي الإبل والبقر والغنم وقيد بالمواشي احترازاً عن النساء والصبيان التي يشق إخراجها فإنها تترك في أرض خربة حتى يموتوا جوعاً كيلا يعودوا حرباً علينا لأن النساء يقع بهن النسل، وأما الصبيان فإنهم يبلغون فيصيرون حرباً علينا ؛ كذا في فتاوى الولوالجي. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه أقوى من القتل المنهي عنه في قتل النساء والصبيان اللهم إلا أن يضطروا إلى ذلك بسبب عدم الحمل فيتركوا ضرورة وهو عجيب منه لأن الولوالجي صرح بأنه يفعل بالنساء والصبيان ذلك عند عدم إمكان الإخراج لا مطلقاً فلا إشكال أصلاً والمسألة مذكورة في المحيط أيضاً وذكر بعده ولهذا قال علماؤنا : إذا وجد المسلمون حية أو عقرباً في دار الحرب في رحالهم ينزعون ذنب العقرب وأنياب الحية قطعاً للضرر عن أنفسهم ولا يقتلونها لأن فيه منفعة الكفار وقد أمرنا بضده .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : نساء من أهل الإسلام متن في دار الحرب فيطأ أهل الحرب النساء الأموات :قال يسعنا أن نحرقهن بالنار اهـ.
The Book of Siyar / Chapter of Spoils and Their Division. Livestock whose extraction is difficult, so they are slaughtered and burned. Division of spoils in their land is not for deposit, nor selling them before that. And they are not to be ransomed with weapons. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And the apparent of al-Walwalji is that it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives with weapons and horses by agreement. His statement: (And the hamstringing of livestock whose extraction is difficult, so they are slaughtered and burned) i.e., the hamstringing of livestock is prohibited because it is mutilation. So he slaughters them because slaughtering an animal is permissible for a valid purpose, and no purpose is more valid than breaking the strength of the enemies. Then they are burned with fire to cut off their benefit from the disbelievers, and it becomes like demolishing buildings, unlike burning before slaughter because it is prohibited. He said in al-Muhit: 'And he indicated that weapons and goods are burned if their transport is difficult, and what does not burn of them is buried in a place where the disbelievers will not come across it, to nullify the benefit for them.' He said in al-Mughrib: 'Aqara ya'qiru 'aqran means he wounded him, and 'aqr of the she-camel with the sword is striking her legs.' Al-Mawashi is the plural of mashi, which are camels, cows, and sheep. The restriction to livestock is to exclude women and children whose extraction is difficult, for they are left in a ruined land until they die of hunger so that they do not become hostile to us again, because women give birth, and as for children, they will grow up and become hostile to us. Thus in Fatawa al-Walwalji. And he criticized it in Fath al-Qadir, saying it is stronger than the prohibited killing of women and children, unless they are compelled to that due to lack of carrying capacity, so they are left out of necessity. And it is strange from him because al-Walwalji explicitly stated that this is done to women and children when removal is not possible, not absolutely, so there is no problem at all. The issue is also mentioned in al-Muhit, and after it he mentioned: 'For this reason our scholars said: If Muslims find a snake or scorpion in the land of war in their baggage, they remove the scorpion's stinger and the snake's fangs to cut off harm from themselves, but they do not kill them because there is benefit for the disbelievers in them, and we have been commanded to oppose that.' End quote. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'Women from the people of Islam who die in the land of war, and the people of war have intercourse with the dead women: He said: It is permissible for us to burn them with fire.' End quote.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining the ruling on disposing of enemy property that cannot be transported. The author begins by clarifying the matn: livestock that are difficult to extract should be slaughtered and burned, not hamstrung, because hamstringing is a form of mutilation (muthla) which is haram. Slaughtering is permissible for a valid purpose, and breaking the enemy's strength is the most valid purpose. Burning after slaughter is allowed to prevent the enemy from benefiting, analogous to demolishing buildings. However, burning before slaughter is prohibited. The commentary then addresses the treatment of women and children: if they cannot be transported, they are left in a ruined land to die from hunger, but they are not directly killed. This is based on the principle that direct killing of women and children is prohibited unless necessary. The author defends al-Walwalji's position against Fath al-Qadir's criticism. An interesting subsidiary ruling is given about snakes and scorpions: Muslims should only remove their harmful parts, not kill them, because the animals' bodies would benefit the enemy. Finally, a fatwa on dead Muslim women: if enemy soldiers violate their corpses, it is permissible to burn the bodies to prevent this desecration.

Key Terms
نساء (nisā'): Women of the enemy in dar al-harb.
صبيان (ṣibyān): Children of the enemy, minors who are non-combatants.
أرض خربة (arḍ khariba): A ruined or barren land where survival is unlikely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the justification for leaving enemy women and children to die indirectly?
A) It is a form of collective punishment.
B) It prevents them from becoming future combatants.
C) It is because they are non-Muslim.
D) It is commanded by the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Indirectly leaving enemy women and children to die is permissible only when extraction is impossible, based on preventing future hostility.

The Prohibition of Dividing Spoils in Dar al-Harb and Its Exceptions
Commentary on prohibition of dividing spoils in enemy territory except for deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb, explain the dalil from hadith and the principle of iḥrāz, and apply the exceptions for deposit and ijtihad/need.

Core Idea
No ownership before Iḥrāz: division in Dar al-Harb is haram, except as deposit or with ijtihad/need.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling that dividing spoils (ghanima) in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) is generally prohibited, based on a prophetic prohibition and the principle that ownership is not established until the spoils are safely conveyed to Dar al-Islam (iḥrāz). However, the text also discusses important exceptions: division for deposit (qismat al-īdāʿ) is permissible, and division performed with ijtihad or due to necessity can be valid. The commentary further explores the nature of joint ownership among soldiers and its effect on actions like freeing slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Identify what act is being discussed: dividing spoils (ghanima) in Dar al-Harb. State the general ruling: it is haram (prohibited) except for deposit. Note that the ruling is expressed as 'haram' rather than 'invalid' to allow for possible validity under certain conditions.
The act is 'qismat ghaneemat fi dar harb' (division of spoils in enemy territory).
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is a prophetic prohibition of selling spoils in Dar al-Harb. Since division is a sale in meaning, it falls under this prohibition. Also, the Hanafi principle that no ownership exists before iḥrāz (conveyance to Dar al-Islam) supports the prohibition.
The hadith is referenced as 'nahi 'an bay' al-ghanaim fi dar al-harb'.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The prohibition on selling indicates that any transaction transferring ownership (like division) is similarly prohibited. Additionally, because ownership is not established until iḥrāz, any division before that is invalid as it purports to transfer something not owned.
Division is considered 'bay' ma'nan' (sale in meaning).
4
Note the Exception: Deposit Division
Division for deposit (qismat īdāʿ) is permissible. This is when the imam lacks transport and divides the spoils temporarily so soldiers can carry them to Dar al-Islam, with the understanding that ownership will be finalized later. The imam can compel soldiers to carry for fair wages.
This exception is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Analyze the Ijtihad/Need Exception
The text clarifies that if a commander divides spoils in Dar al-Harb with ijtihad (independent reasoning) or due to the genuine need of the soldiers, the division is valid. Otherwise, it is invalid. This explains why the text says 'haram' instead of 'batil' (invalid) — to allow for this exception.
Ijtihad here means the commander believes the division is necessary and permissible under the circumstances.
6
Distinguish General vs. Specific Joint Ownership
After division by subunits (raayāt/arāfa), if the group is small (around 100 or less, or 40), the joint ownership is specific (shirka khāṣṣa), allowing individual soldiers to free slaves or make them umm walad. If the group is large, the ownership is general (shirka ʿāmma), and such actions are not valid without the consent of all co-owners. The preferred view leaves the determination to the imam's ijtihad.
This affects practical matters like freeing a slave from the spoils before formal division in Dar al-Islam.

كتاب السير باب الغنائم وقسمتها
من السبي ادعاه بعض الغانمين قبله ويجب عقرها وتقسم الأمة والولد والعقر بين الغانمين، ولا يورث نصيب من مات قبله ولا ضمان على من أتلف شيئاً من الغنيمة قبله؛ كذا ذكره الشارح وغيره، وظاهره أن جميع تلك الأحكام إنما قبله، أما بعده فالأحكام مختلفة وليس كذلك فإنه لا ملك بعد الإحراز بدار الإسلام أيضاً إلا بالقسم بدار الإسلام فلا يثبت بالإحراز ملك لأحد بل يتأكد الحق، ولهذا لو أعتق واحد من الغانمين عبداً بعد الإحراز لا يعتق، ولو كان هناك ملك مشترك عتق بعتق الشريك ويجري فيه ما عرف في عتق الشريك، فحكم استيلاد الجارية بعد الإحراز قبل القسمة وقبله سواء. نعم لو قسمت تلك الغنيمة على الرايات أو العرافة فوقعت جارية بين أهل راية صح استيلاد أحدهم لها فإنه يصح عتقه لها لأنها مشتركة بينه وبين أهل تلك الراية والعرافة شركة ملك لكن هذا إذا قلوا حتى تكون الشركة خاصة، أما إذا كثروا فلا لأن بالشركة العامة لا تثبت ولاية الإعتاق. والقليل مائة أو أقل، وقيل أربعون .
قال في المبسوط والأولى أن لا يوقت ويجعل موكولاً إلى اجتهاد الإمام؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي التتارخانية قال المتأخرون : وأحسن ما قيل فيه إن الجند إذا كان بحيث تقع بهم الشركة في الأغلب كانت الشركة فيما بينهم عامة، وإن كانت بحيث لا تقع بهم الشركة في الغالب تكون شركة خاصة .اهـ. وفيها وفي المنتقى قال أبو يوسف : إذا أعتق الإمام عبداً من الخمس جاز عتقه وولاؤه لجماعة المسلمين وليس له أن يوالي أحداً اهـ. وفي المحيط : ولو وطئ جارية لا يجد ويؤخذ منه العقران وطئها في دار الإسلام دون دار الحرب لأنه أتلف منافع بضعها اهـ. وهذا هو الظاهر لأن الوطء في دار الحرب لا يجب فيه شيء. وقد نقله في التتارخانية بصيغة قال محمد فكان هو المذهب قال : وكذا إذا قتل واحداً من السبي أو استهلك شيئاً من الغنيمة في دار الحرب فلا ضمان عليه لا فرق بين أن يكون المستهلك من الغانمين أو غيرهم. وعبر بالحرمة دون الصحة لأنه إذا قسم في دار الحرب مجتهداً أو قسم لحاجة الغانمين ،فصحيحة، وإن قسم بلا اجتهاد أو اجتهد فوقع على عدم صحتها فغير صحيحة. وقيد بغير الإيداع لأنها للإيداع جائزة، وصورتها أن لا يكون للإمام من بيت المال حمولة يحمل عليها الغنائم فيقسمها بين الغانمين قسمة إيداع ليحملها إلى دار الإسلام ثم يرتجعها منهم فيها، فإن أبوا أن يحملوها أجبرهم على ذلك بأجر المثل في رواية السير الكبير لأنه دفع ضرر عام بتحميل ضرر خاص كما لو استأجر دابة شهراً فمضت المدة في المفازة أو استأجر سفينة فمضت المدة في وسط البحر فإنه ينعقد عليها إجارة أخرى بأجر المثل، ولا فتأمل قوله : (ويجب عقرها سيذكر في هذه القولة ما يخالفه قوله : فكان هو المذهب) أفاد أن ما قدمه عن الشارح الزيلعي خلاف المذهب قوله : (ولا) يجبرهم في رواية السير الصغير) قال في الفتح :
His statement: (And if some of the people of war become Muslims in their land, it will be mentioned at the statement of the matn 'la al-suqiy' what contradicts it.) His statement: (And division of spoils in their land is not for deposit) i.e., division of spoils in the land of war for other than deposit is prohibited because of the prohibition on selling spoils in the land of war, and division is a sale in meaning, so it falls under it. And because taking possession establishes a protective and transferable hand, and the second is absent due to their ability to recapture and its apparent presence. And the principle with us is that there is no ownership before conveyance to dar al-Islam, so division and sale before it are prohibited. And reinforcements participate with the army before it, even if some of the people of war become Muslims in their land before they are captured. And the lineage of a slave woman's child from the captives is not established if some of the spoilers claim it before that, and her hamstringing is obligatory, and the slave woman, the child, and the compensation are divided among the spoilers. And the share of one who dies before that is not inherited, and there is no liability on one who destroys something of the spoils before that. Thus the commentator and others mentioned it. And its apparent is that all these rulings are only before that. As for after that, the rulings are different, but it is not so, for there is no ownership after conveyance to dar al-Islam either, except by division in dar al-Islam. So no one acquires ownership by conveyance; rather the right becomes confirmed. For this reason, if one of the spoilers frees a slave after conveyance, it does not become free. And if there was joint ownership, it would be freed by the partner's freeing, and the known rules of freeing a partner apply. So the ruling on umm walad of a slave woman after conveyance before division and before it is the same. Yes, if those spoils are divided by banners or units and a slave woman falls to the people of one banner, it is valid for one of them to make her umm walad, for his freeing of her is valid because she is shared between him and the people of that banner, and that unit is a joint ownership. But this is if they are few so that the ownership is specific. As for when they are many, then it is not valid because with general joint ownership, the authority of freeing is not established. And few is one hundred or less, and it is said forty. He said in al-Mabsut: 'And the preferable is not to set a limit and to leave it to the imam's ijtihad.' Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya, the later scholars said: 'The best of what is said about it is that if the soldiers are such that joint ownership occurs among them in most cases, then the joint ownership among them is general; and if it is such that joint ownership does not occur among them in most cases, then it is specific.' End quote. And in it and in al-Muntaqa, Abu Yusuf said: 'If the imam frees a slave from the khums, his freeing is valid, and his wala is for the entire Muslim community, and he may not assign wala to anyone.' End quote. And in al-Muhit: 'And if one has intercourse with a slave woman, he is not liable, but the compensation for her and the mahr must be taken; he has intercourse in dar al-Islam but not in dar al-Harb, because he has destroyed the benefits of her private parts.' End quote. And this is apparent because intercourse in dar al-Harb does not entail anything. And it has been transmitted in al-Tatarkhaniyya in the wording of Muhammad, so it is the madhhab. He said: 'Similarly, if one kills a captive or consumes something of the spoils in dar al-Harb, there is no liability, whether the consumer is from the spoilers or others.' And he used 'prohibition' rather than 'invalidity' because if he divides in dar al-Harb as a mujtahid or due to the need of the spoilers, it is valid; but if he divides without ijtihad or ijtihad but it turns out to be incorrect, then it is invalid. And it is restricted to other than deposit because division for deposit is permissible. Its form is that the imam does not have from the treasury transport to carry the spoils, so he divides them among the spoilers as a deposit division for them to carry to dar al-Islam, then he takes them back from them there. If they refuse to carry them, he compels them to do so with the wages of the like in the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir because it is repelling a general harm by imposing a specific harm, just as if one rents an animal for a month and the period passes in the desert, or rents a ship and the period passes in the middle of the sea, then another hire with the wages of the like is contracted over it. And consider his statement: (And its hamstringing is obligatory, it will be mentioned in this statement what contradicts it. His statement: 'So it is the madhhab') indicated that what he presented from the commentator al-Zayla'i is contrary to the madhhab. His statement: (And he does not compel them in the narration of al-Siyar al-Saghir) He said in al-Fath:
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of dividing spoils (ghanima) in dar al-Harb. The author first addresses a cross-reference: a point about a person from dar al-Harb who embraces Islam in his own land will be discussed later. The main ruling: dividing spoils in dar al-Harb for any purpose except deposit is prohibited. This is based on a prophetic prohibition of selling spoils in dar al-Harb, and division is considered a sale in meaning. Additionally, no ownership is established until the spoils are safely brought to dar al-Islam; possession in dar al-Harb only confers a protective right, not a transferable right, because the enemy can recapture them. Therefore, both division and sale before conveyance are haram. Reinforcements that join the army before conveyance also share in the spoils, even if they were originally from dar al-Harb and became Muslim before being captured. The commentary then clarifies that all rulings (e.g., inheritance, liability for destroying spoils) apply before division, but even after conveyance to dar al-Islam, ownership is not established until formal division. For example, if a soldier frees a slave after conveying spoils to dar al-Islam, the freeing is ineffective because the slave is still jointly owned by all soldiers. However, if the spoils are divided by subunits (raayāt or arāfa), then within a small subunit, a soldier can validly set a slave woman as umm walad or free her, because the joint ownership is specific. The text discusses the criteria for general vs. specific joint ownership: if the group is small (100 or less, or 40 according to some), ownership is specific; otherwise, it is general. The preferred view is to leave the determination to the imam’s discretion. Further, Abu Yusuf states that if the imam frees a slave from the khums, the wala goes to the Muslim community. Also, intercourse with a captive slave woman in dar al-Islam requires compensation for her benefits, but not in dar al-Harb. Destroying spoils in dar al-Harb incurs no penalty. The ruling is expressed as 'prohibited' rather than 'invalid' because if the imam divides with ijtihad or due to necessity, the division is valid. Finally, the exception for deposit is explained: if the imam lacks means to transport spoils, he can divide them as a deposit for soldiers to carry, then retrieve them in dar al-Islam. Soldiers can be compelled to carry with wages.

Key Terms
إحراز (iḥrāz): Conveyance of spoils to a safe place in dar al-Islam, establishing control and ownership rights.
قسمة إيداع (qismat īdāʿ): A temporary division of spoils as a deposit, not transferring ownership, for the purpose of transport.
شركة خاصة (shirka khāṣṣa): Specific joint ownership among a small group of soldiers, allowing individual acts like freeing a slave.
شركة عامة (shirka ʿāmma): General joint ownership among a large group, where no individual has authority to act unilaterally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is division of spoils in Dar al-Harb considered valid?
A) Always valid, regardless of circumstances
B) Valid only if performed as a deposit (إيداع) or with ijtihad/necessity
C) Never valid
D) Valid only if the imam personally performs it

Key Takeaway
Division of spoils in Dar al-Harb is generally prohibited until iḥrāz, except as a deposit or when necessitated by ijtihad or need; this reflects the Hanafi balance between strict principle and practical necessity.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Freeing or Impregnating a Captive Before Division of Spoils
Ruling and commentary on the effect of claiming a captive before division of spoils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing a slave or performing istilad on a captive woman after ihraz but before division, and identify the exceptional condition that makes such acts valid.

Core Idea
No individual ownership after ihraz; only a collective right, so freeing is invalid until actual division.

This lesson examines a crucial ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding spoils of war: after the spoils are brought into Dar al-Islam (ihraz), does each soldier own his share? The passage clarifies that ownership is not established until division; only a right is confirmed. Consequently, any disposal of a share—such as freeing a slave or making a captive woman a umm walad—is invalid before division, with one significant exception: when the spoils have been divided among small groups (like banners) where partnership is specific.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its General Ruling
The passage begins with a ruling from Kanz al-Daqā’iq: if a soldier claims a captive woman before division, he must pay 'aqr, and the woman, child, and 'aqr are divided among all ghānimīn. Also, the share of a deceased soldier is not inherited, and no liability for damage before division. These rules apply before division.
The key point is that all these rulings are based on the absence of individual ownership.
2
Understand the Principle of Iḥrāz
The commentator clarifies that even after ihraz (bringing spoils into Dar al-Islam), ownership is not established for any individual. Only a collective right (ḥaqq) is confirmed. Therefore, freeing a slave after ihraz but before division is invalid (lā ya‘tiq), unlike in common ownership where a partner can free.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may view ihraz as transferring ownership.
3
Recognize the Exception: Division Among Small Groups
If the spoils are divided among banners (rayāt) or army sections (‘arāfah) before the general division, and a slave woman falls to a small group, then a soldier from that group can validly free or perform istilad. This is because the group has proprietary partnership (shirkat milk).
The validity hinges on the group being small ('qalīl') so that the partnership is specific (khāṣṣa), not general (‘āmma).
4
Apply the Criterion for 'Small Group'
The passage gives two opinions: one hundred or less, or forty. The preferred view in al-Mabsūṭ is not to set a fixed number but to leave it to the imam's ijtihad. Later scholars in al-Tātārkhāniyya define the criterion based on custom: if the group usually shares property among themselves, it is a general partnership (freeing invalid); if not, it is specific (freeing valid).
This is a practical tool for muftis to determine the ruling based on the army structure.

هي من السبي ادعاه بعض الغانمين قبله ويجب عقرها وتقسم الأمة والولد والعقر بين الغانمين، ولا يورث نصيب من مات قبله ولا ضمان على من أتلف شيئاً من الغنيمة قبله؛ كذا ذكره الشارح وغيره، وظاهره أن جميع تلك الأحكام إنما قبله، أما بعده فالأحكام مختلفة وليس كذلك فإنه لا ملك بعد الإحراز بدار الإسلام أيضاً إلا بالقسم بدار الإسلام فلا يثبت بالإحراز ملك لأحد بل يتأكد الحق، ولهذا لو أعتق واحد من الغانمين عبداً بعد الإحراز لا يعتق، ولو كان هناك ملك مشترك عتق بعتق الشريك ويجري فيه ما عرف في عتق الشريك، فحكم استيلاد الجارية بعد الإحراز قبل القسمة وقبله سواء. نعم لو قسمت تلك الغنيمة على الرايات أو العرافة فوقعت جارية بين أهل راية صح استيلاد أحدهم لها فإنه يصح عتقه لها لأنها مشتركة بينه وبين أهل تلك الراية والعرافة شركة ملك لكن هذا إذا قلوا حتى تكون الشركة خاصة، أما إذا كثروا فلا لأن بالشركة العامة لا تثبت ولاية الإعتاق. والقليل مائة أو أقل، وقيل أربعون .
قال في المبسوط والأولى أن لا يوقت ويجعل موكولاً إلى اجتهاد الإمام؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي التتارخانية قال المتأخرون : وأحسن ما قيل فيه إن الجند إذا كان بحيث تقع بهم الشركة في الأغلب كانت الشركة فيما بينهم عامة، وإن كانت بحيث لا تقع بهم الشركة في الغالب تكون شركة خاصة .اهـ.
She (the captive woman) from the captives is claimed by some of the ghānimīn before division, and her 'aqr (indemnity) is obligatory, and the slave woman, the child, and the 'aqr are divided among the ghānimīn. And the share of one who died before (division) is not inherited, and there is no liability on anyone who destroys anything from the spoils before (division). Thus the commentator and others mentioned it. And its apparent meaning is that all those rulings are only before it. As for after it, the rulings are different, but it is not so, because there is no ownership after ihraz (taking to Dar al-Islam) either except by division in Dar al-Islam. So by ihraz, ownership is not established for anyone, but the right is confirmed. For this reason, if one of the ghānimīn frees a slave after ihraz, it does not take effect. And if there were common ownership, it would take effect by the freeing of the partner, and what is known in the freeing of a partner applies. So the ruling of istilad (intercourse for childbearing) of the slave girl after ihraz before division and before it is the same. Yes, if those spoils are divided among the banners (rayāt) or the ‘arāfah (groups), and a slave girl falls among the people of a banner, the istilad of one of them for her is valid, and his freeing of her is valid because she is jointly owned between him and the people of that banner and ‘arāfah in joint ownership. But this is if they are few so that the partnership is specific; but if they are many, then not, because with general partnership, the authority of freeing is not established. And ‘few’ is a hundred or less, and it is said forty. He said in al-Mabsūṭ: and the preferable is not to set a limit and to leave it to the ijtihad of the imam. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And in al-Tātārkhāniyya: the later scholars said: the best of what has been said about it is that if the army is such that partnership among them usually occurs, then the partnership among them is general, and if it is such that partnership among them usually does not occur, then it is specific. End.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary from Sharḥ al-Zayla‘ī and other sources. It begins with a matn ruling from Kanz al-Daqā’iq: if a ghānī claims a captive woman before division of spoils, he must pay her ‘aqr (indemnity for using her), and the woman, her child, and the ‘aqr are divided among all the ghānimīn. Other rules: the share of a ghānī who dies before division is not inherited (since ownership is not yet established), and no one is liable for damaging spoils before division. The commentator clarifies that these rules apply only before ihraz (taking spoils into Dār al-Islām). After ihraz, ownership is still not established until division; only a collective right (ḥaqq) is confirmed. Therefore, freeing a slave after ihraz is invalid (lā ya‘tiq), unlike common ownership where freeing by one partner is effective. Similarly, istilād (making a slave girl a umm walad) after ihraz is not valid. However, if the spoils are divided among banners (rayāt) or ‘arāfah (army sections) before division of the whole, and a slave falls to a small group, then a soldier can validly free or have istilād with her, because the group has proprietary partnership (shirkat milk). This validity depends on the group being small (qalīl) so the partnership is specific (khāṣṣa), not general (‘āmma). The definition of qalīl: some say 100 or less, some say 40; the preferred view leaves it to the imam’s ijtihad. Later scholars in al-Tātārkhāniyya say the criterion is whether the group usually shares property among themselves: if yes, partnership is general (freeing invalid); if no, it is specific (freeing valid). The legal reasoning is based on the distinction between confirmed right and full ownership, and the analogy to common property is distinguished.

Key Terms
إحراز (iḥrāz): Taking spoils into Dār al-Islām, which confirms a right but not full ownership until division.
عقر (‘aqr): Indemnity paid for using a captive woman's sexual services, equal to her mahr.
الشركة العامة والشركة الخاصة (al-shirkat al-‘āmmah wa al-shirkat al-khāṣṣah): General partnership: a large group where members typically share property, so no individual authority to free. Specific partnership: a small group where members do not typically share, so individuals can act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a soldier frees a slave from the spoils after the spoils have been brought into Dār al-Islām but before distribution, what is the ruling?
A) The freeing is valid because the spoils belong to the soldiers.
B) The freeing is invalid because ownership is not yet established.
C) The freeing is valid only if the soldier is the commander.
D) The freeing is valid only if the slave is from the khums.

Key Takeaway
After spoils are brought into Dar al-Islam, individual ownership is not established until division; thus freeing or istilad before division is invalid unless the spoils have been divided among a small group where partnership is specific.

Miscellaneous Rulings on Spoils in Hanafi Fiqh
Presenting rulings on imam freeing from khums, intercourse with captives, damage in Dar al-Harb, and division validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the imam's freeing from khums, liability for intercourse with captives, damage to spoils in Dar al-Harb, the validity of division, and the deposit division with forced carriage.

Core Idea
Location determines liability: actions on spoils in Dar al-Harb incur no liability; division requires ijtihad or need.

The management of spoils of war involves numerous legal details. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq gathers several key rulings: the imam's freedom to free slaves from the khums, the liability (or lack thereof) for sexual intercourse with captives, and the conditions for dividing spoils in enemy territory. These rules illustrate the Hanafi school's practical approach to ensuring justice and preserving the common good.

Guided Path
1
Identify each independent ruling
The passage presents four distinct rulings: (a) imam freeing from khums, (b) intercourse with captives, (c) killing/consuming spoils in Dar al-Harb, (d) division in Dar al-Harb. List them separately.
Each ruling has its own conditions and exceptions.
2
Analyze the rationale (ta'lil) for each
For rulings (b) and (c), the reason is that ownership is not fully established in Dar al-Harb. For (d), division is valid if based on ijtihad or necessity. The deposit division is an exception to the prohibition.
Understanding the rationale helps in applying analogous cases.
3
Examine the deposit division exception and the qiyas for forced carriage
The imam may make a temporary deposit division to transport spoils if no transport is available. If soldiers refuse to carry, they can be forced with compensation, analogized to hire contracts that extend beyond term.
This qiyas is istihsan based on repelling general harm.
4
Reflect on the intra-madhhab difference regarding 'aqr and forced carriage
The commentator notes that the earlier view (al-Zayla'i) that 'aqr is always obligatory contradicts the relied-upon madhhab, which distinguishes Dar al-Harb from Dar al-Islam. Similarly, there is a difference between al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Siyar al-Saghir on forcing soldiers to carry.
The later position (mufta bihi) is the one that differentiates based on location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المنتقى قال أبو يوسف : إذا أعتق الإمام عبداً من الخمس جاز عتقه وولاؤه لجماعة المسلمين وليس له أن يوالي أحداً اهـ. وفي المحيط : ولو وطئ جارية لا يجد ويؤخذ منه العقران وطئها في دار الإسلام دون دار الحرب لأنه أتلف منافع بضعها اهـ. وهذا هو الظاهر لأن الوطء في دار الحرب لا يجب فيه شيء. وقد نقله في التتارخانية بصيغة قال محمد قال : وكذا إذا قتل واحداً من السبي أو استهلك شيئاً من الغنيمة في دار الحرب فلا ضمان عليه لا فرق بين أن يكون المستهلك من الغانمين أو غيرهم. وعبر بالحرمة دون الصحة لأنه إذا قسم في دار الحرب مجتهداً أو قسم لحاجة الغانمين ،فصحيحة، وإن قسم بلا اجتهاد أو اجتهد فوقع على عدم صحتها فغير صحيحة. وقيد بغير الإيداع لأنها للإيداع جائزة، وصورتها أن لا يكون للإمام من بيت المال حمولة يحمل عليها الغنائم فيقسمها بين الغانمين قسمة إيداع ليحملها إلى دار الإسلام ثم يرتجعها منهم فيها، فإن أبوا أن يحملوها أجبرهم على ذلك بأجر المثل في رواية السير الكبير لأنه دفع ضرر عام بتحميل ضرر خاص كما لو استأجر دابة شهراً فمضت المدة في المفازة أو استأجر سفينة فمضت المدة في وسط البحر فإنه ينعقد عليها إجارة أخرى بأجر المثل، ولا فتأمل قوله : (ويجب عقرها سيذكر في هذه القولة ما يخالفه قوله : فكان هو المذهب) أفاد أن ما قدمه عن الشارح الزيلعي خلاف المذهب قوله : (ولا) يجبرهم في رواية السير الصغير) قال في الفتح :
And in al-Muntaqā, Abū Yūsuf said: If the imam frees a slave from the khums, his freeing is valid and his walā’ (patronage) belongs to the general body of Muslims, and he may not give allegiance to anyone [specific]. End. And in al-Muḥīṭ: If someone has intercourse with a slave girl (from spoils) without finding (another avenue), the two ‘aqrs are taken from him for intercourse in Dār al-Islām, but not in Dār al-Ḥarb, because he destroyed the benefits of her pudendum. End. And this is apparent because intercourse in Dār al-Ḥarb entails no obligation. And it was transmitted in al-Tātārkhāniyya in the wording of Muḥammad: he said: Likewise, if someone kills a captive or consumes something from the spoils in Dār al-Ḥarb, there is no liability upon him, there being no difference between whether the consumer is from the ghānimīn or others. And he expressed (the ruling) in terms of prohibition (ḥurmah) not validity (ṣiḥḥah), because if he divides (spoils) in Dār al-Ḥarb with ijtihād or divides due to the need of the ghānimīn, it is valid. And if he divides without ijtihād, or exercises ijtihād but it results in invalidity, then it is not valid. And he qualified (the prohibition) with other than deposit (īdā‘), because deposit division is permissible. Its form is: the imam does not have transport from the treasury to carry the spoils, so he makes a deposit division among the ghānimīn for them to carry to Dār al-Islām and then takes it back from them there. If they refuse to carry it, he forces them to do so with compensation equivalent to the hire (ujr al-mithl) in the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabīr, because it is repelling a general harm by imposing a specific harm, just as if one hires an animal for a month and the period expires while in the desert, or hires a ship and the period expires in mid-sea, then another hire contract is concluded with equivalent hire. And reflect on his statement: 'And the ‘aqr is obligatory' – he will mention later in this passage what contradicts it – his statement: 'so it is the madhhab' indicates that what he presented from al-Shāriḥ al-Zayla‘ī is contrary to the madhhab. His statement: '(and not) he forces them in the narration of al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr' – he said in al-Fatḥ:
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage collects several independent rulings related to spoils. First, from al-Muntaqā: Abū Yūsuf rules that if the imam frees a slave from the khums (the one-fifth share of the spoils belonging to the state), the freeing is valid, but the walā’ (clientage) goes to the entire Muslim community, not to any individual. Second, from al-Muḥīṭ: if someone has intercourse with a captive slave woman (after ihraz but before division?), he must pay two ‘aqrs (indemnities) for intercourse in Dār al-Islām, but not in Dār al-Ḥarb. The reason is that in Dār al-Ḥarb, no liability arises because ownership is not yet secured. The clear rule is that only intercourse in Dār al-Islām incurs ‘aqr. Third, from al-Tātārkhāniyya via Muḥammad: if someone kills a captive or destroys spoils in Dār al-Ḥarb, there is no liability, whether the person is a ghānī or not. Fourth, discussing division in Dār al-Ḥarb: it is permissible if the imam exercises ijtihād or if there is a need (like fear of loss). If he divides without ijtihād or his ijtihād leads to invalidity, the division is invalid. However, division by way of deposit (qismat īdā‘) is always valid: this occurs when the imam has no transport, so he distributes the spoils as a deposit for carriers, and then takes them back in Dār al-Islām. Soldiers can be forced to carry spoils with compensation (ujr al-mithl) based on an analogy to hiring contracts that extend beyond term in desert or sea. The passage ends with a meta-commentary pointing out that the earlier statement from al-Zayla‘ī (that ‘aqr is obligatory) is actually contrary to the relied-upon madhhab (which distinguishes between Dār al-Ḥarb and Dār al-Islām). And on forcing soldiers to carry, there is a difference between the narrations of al-Siyar al-Kabīr (force with compensation) and al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr (no force) – the latter is explained in al-Fatḥ as consistent because one cannot force initial hire, but the former is about continuation.

Key Terms
الخمس (al-khums): The one-fifth share of spoils that goes to the imam for the public treasury (Bayt al-Māl).
العقر (al-‘aqr): Indemnity for sexual intercourse with a female captive, equal to her mahr.
قسمة الإيداع (qismat al-īdā‘): A temporary division of spoils as a deposit for carriers, not as ownership transfer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a soldier kills a captive from the spoils while still in Dār al-Ḥarb, what is the ruling?
A) He must pay compensation (ḍamān) to the other ghānimīn.
B) There is no liability because ownership is not established in Dār al-Ḥarb.
C) He is liable only if he was not a ghānī.
D) He must pay blood money (diyah).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school carefully delineates liability based on location (Dār al-Ḥarb vs Dār al-Islām) and ensures flexibility in dividing spoils through ijtihad and deposit division.

Share of Reinforcements in Spoils
Defining the share of reinforcements and who is excluded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which reinforcements (al-madd wa al-rid’) share in spoils, and identify who is excluded from sharing.

Core Idea
Reinforcements share only if they join before iḥrāz; all participants are equal in the sabab.

This passage outlines the Hanafi ruling on the share of auxiliary troops (al-rid’ wal-madd) in spoils. The core principle is that entitlement is based on crossing the border into enemy territory or witnessing the battle, regardless of actual fighting. Therefore, even the sick, the commander, and volunteers share equally, while traders and those who join after the spoils are brought to Islamic territory do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Determine the legal situation: auxiliary forces (reinforcements) arriving after the battle has started but before the spoils are secured.
2
Determine the cause (sabab) for entitlement
The cause is crossing the border (mujāwazah) or witnessing the battle (shuhūd al-waq‘ah). Those who have not crossed, like traders, are not entitled.
This is the basis for equality among all fighters.
3
Apply the timing condition
Reinforcements share only if they join while the spoils are still in Dār al-Ḥarb and before iḥrāz (taking to Dār al-Islām) or before the imam's division or sale in Dār al-Ḥarb.
After iḥrāz, their right is cut off.
4
List those excluded
Al-sūqī (market-goer), one who dies before division, and reinforcements arriving after iḥrāz do not share.
5
Note the equality principle
All participants share equally—fighter, ill, commander, volunteer—because they share the same sabab.
This is without disagreement in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرك الردء والمدد فيها لا السوقي بلا قتال ولا من مات فيها وبعد الإحراز بدارنا
يجبرهم في رواية السير الصغير لأنه لا يجبر على عقد الإجارة ابتداء كما إذا نفقت دابته في المفازة ومع رفيقه دابة لا يجبر على الإجارة بخلاف ما استشهد به فإنه بناء وليس بابتداء وهو أسهل منه، ولو كان في بيت المال أو في الغنيمة حمولة حمل عليها لأن الكل ما لهم. وفي الخانية : ولو أن الإمام أودع الغنيمة إلى بعض الجند قبل القسمة ولا يبين ما فعل حتى مات لا يضمن شيئاً. وفي السير الكبير : وإذا أراد أمير العسكر أن يرسل رسولاً من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام بشيء من أموال المسلمين ولم يقدر الرسول أن يخرج إلا فارساً ولبعض العسكر فضل فرس فلا بأس بأخذ فرسه على كره منه .اهـ. قوله : ( وبيعها قبلها) أي حرم بيع الغنائم قبل القسمة. أطلقه فشمل ما قبل الإحراز وما بعده أما قبله لم يملكه، وأما بعده فنصيبه مجهول فلا يمكنه أن وقد ورد النهي عن البيع قبل القسمة كما قدمناه قوله: (وشرك يبيع الردء والمدد فيها أي في الغنيمة لاستوائهم في السبب وهو المجاوزة أو شهود الوقعة، وإذا المدد في دار الحرب قبل أن يخرجوا الغنيمة إلى دار الإسلام شاركوهم فيها على ما الأصل. وإنما ينقطع حق المشاركة عندنا بالإحراز أو بقسمة الإمام في دار الحرب قدمناه أو ببيعه المغانم فيها لأن بكل منها يتم الملك فتنقطع شركة المدد والردء ـ بكسر الراء وسكون الدال المهملة بعدها همزة - بمعنى العون والمدد الجماعة الناصرون للجند. وأفاد المصنف أن المقاتل وغيره سواء حتى يستحق الجندي الذي لم يقاتل لمرض أو غيره، وأنه لا يتميز على آخر بشيء حتى أمير العسكر وهذا بلا خلاف لاستواء الكل في سبب الاستحقاق ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي المحيط : المتطوع في الغزو وصاحب الديوان في الغنيمة سواء اهـ. وفي

واحد
والأوجه أنه إن خاف تفرقهم لو قسمها قسمة الغنيمة يفعل هذا وإن لم يخف قسمها قسمة الغنيمة في دار الحرب فإنها تصح للحاجة وفيه إسقاط الإكراه وإسقاط الأجرة. قوله : (وبيعها قبلها) قال في الفتح: وهذا في بيع الغزاة ظاهر، وأما بيع الإمام لها فذكر الطحاوي لأنه يصح مجتهد فيه يعني أنه لا بد أن يكون الإمام رأى المصلحة في ذلك وأقله تخفيف إكراه الحمل عن الناس أو عن البهائم ونحوه وتخفيف مؤنته عنهم فيقع عن اجتهاد في المصلحة فلا يقع جزافاً فينعقد بلا كراهة مطلقاً. قوله : (قبل أن يخرجوا الغنيمة إلى دار (الإسلام أي وقبل أن يظهروا على البلد لما في الشرنبلالية عند قول الدرر ومدداً يلحقهم ثمة» : وتقييده لحوق المدد بدار الحرب إشارة إلى أنه لو فتح العسكر بلداً بدار الحرب واستظهروا عليه ثم لحقهم المدد لم يشاركهم لأنه صار بلاد الإسلام فصارت الغنيمة محرزة بدار الإسلام؛ نص عليه في الاختيار اهـ. وعلى هذا فقول المؤلف وإذا لحقهم المدد الخ» مصور فيما إذا غنموا منهم ولم يظهروا عليهم ولم تصر دار إسلام قال في التتارخانية : ولو أن عسكراً دخلوا دار الحرب وقاتلوا أهل المدينة من مدائنهم وقهروا أهلها واستولوا عليها وفتحوها وأظهروا فيها أحكام الإسلام حتى صارت المدينة دار الإسلام ولم يقسموا الغنائم حتى لحقهم المدد لا يشاركوهم فيها اهـ.
And the share of the auxiliary (al-rid’) and the reinforcement (al-madd) in it (the spoils) — not the market-goer (al-sūqī) without fighting, nor one who dies in it, nor after ihraz in our land (Dār al-Islām). He forces them in the narration of al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr, because one is not forced to enter into a hire contract initially, just as if his animal dies in the desert and his companion has an animal, he is not forced to hire — contrary to what was cited as evidence, for that is continuation and not initiation, and it is easier. And if there is transport in the treasury or in the spoils, he loads it on it, because the whole belongs to them. And in al-Khāniyya: If the imam deposits the spoils with some soldiers before division and does not clarify what he did until he dies, he is not liable for anything. And in al-Siyar al-Kabīr: If the commander of the army wants to send a messenger from Dār al-Ḥarb to Dār al-Islām with some wealth of the Muslims, and the messenger can only go as a horseman, and some soldiers have a spare horse, it is permissible to take his horse even against his will. End. His statement: 'And its sale before it' meaning the sale of spoils before division is prohibited (ḥarām). He made it absolute, so it includes before iḥrāz and after it: before it he does not own it, and after it his share is unknown, so he cannot... And the prohibition of sale before division has been reported as we mentioned. His statement: 'And the share of the auxiliary and reinforcement' meaning in the spoils, because they are equal in the cause (sabab), which is crossing the border or witnessing the battle. When the reinforcement is in Dār al-Ḥarb before they take the spoils out to Dār al-Islām, they share with them in it, based on the principle. And the right of sharing is cut off according to us by iḥrāz, or by the imam’s division in Dār al-Ḥarb as we presented, or by his sale of the spoils there, because by each of these ownership is perfected, so the partnership of the reinforcement and auxiliary is cut off. (Rid’: with kasr of rā’ and sukūn of dāl, after it hamza — meaning help. Madd: the group that supports the soldiers.) And the author indicates that the fighter and other are equal, so the soldier who did not fight due to illness or other reason is entitled, and none is distinguished over another by anything, not even the commander — this is without disagreement, because all are equal in the cause of entitlement. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And in al-Muḥīṭ: The volunteer (mutatawwi‘) in battle and the regular soldier (ṣāḥib al-dīwān) are equal in the spoils. End. And it (the text says) 'join them' from him that he is one. And the more appropriate view is that if he fears their dispersal if he divides it as a division of spoils, he does this; if he does not fear, he divides it as a division of spoils in Dār al-Ḥarb, for it is valid due to need, and it involves dropping compulsion and dropping the hire. His statement: 'And its sale before it' — he said in al-Fatḥ: This is apparent in the sale by the ghuzāt; as for the sale by the imam, al-Ṭaḥāwī mentioned that it is valid with ijtihād, meaning the imam must have seen a maslaḥah in it, the least of which is alleviating the burden of carrying from people or animals and the like, and reducing its hardship for them; so it occurs based on ijtihād in maslaḥah, not randomly, so it is concluded without any dislike (karāhah) at all. His statement: 'before they take the spoils to Dār al-Islām' i.e. before they gain control of the town, as in al-Sharnablāliyya at the statement in al-Durar 'and reinforcements join them there': his restricting the joining of reinforcements to Dār al-Ḥarb indicates that if the army conquers a town in Dār al-Ḥarb and gains control over it, then reinforcements join them, they do not share, because it has become Dār al-Islām, so the spoils are considered iḥrāz in Dār al-Islām; this is stated in al-Ikhtiyār. End. And accordingly, the author’s statement 'and if reinforcements join them' etc. is depicted where they ghanīm from them (i.e., captured spoils) but have not yet gained control over them and it has not become Dār al-Islām. He said in al-Tātārkhāniyya: If an army enters Dār al-Ḥarb and fights the people of one of its cities, overpowers them, seizes it, opens it, and establishes the rulings of Islām there until the city becomes Dār al-Islām, and they did not divide the spoils until reinforcements joined them, the reinforcements do not share with them. End.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage deals with two main topics: the share of reinforcements (al-madd wa al-rid’) in spoils, and the prohibition of selling spoils before division. First, reinforcements and auxiliaries share in the spoils if they join the army while still in Dār al-Ḥarb and before the spoils are taken to Dār al-Islām (iḥrāz). The cause (sabab) for entitlement is crossing the border into enemy territory or witnessing the battle itself. Therefore, those who did not fight due to illness or other reason are still entitled, as are the commander and all soldiers equally — there is no distinction. However, a non-fighter who did not cross the border (like a market-trader, al-sūqī) does not share. The right to share is cut off by iḥrāz (bringing spoils to Dār al-Islām), by the imam’s division in Dār al-Ḥarb, or by the imam’s sale of spoils in Dār al-Ḥarb, because each perfects ownership. Importantly, if the army conquers a town and establishes Islām there (making it Dār al-Islām), then even if spoils are not yet divided, reinforcements arriving afterwards do not share, because the spoils are considered iḥrāz in Dār al-Islām. Second, the sale of spoils before division is prohibited (ḥarām) for soldiers, because they do not own their share individually (before iḥrāz) or the share is unknown (after iḥrāz). But the imam may sell spoils before division if he exercises ijtihād and finds a maslaḥah, such as reducing the burden of transportation. This sale is valid without dislike. The passage also includes practical rulings: forcing soldiers to carry spoils with compensation (comparing to hire contracts), and the permissibility of taking a soldier’s horse against his will for a messenger if needed. These are based on the principle of repelling general harm by imposing specific harm.

Key Terms
الردء والمدد (al-rid’ wal-madd): Auxiliary soldiers who join the main army after the battle has started; they share in spoils if they join before iḥrāz.
الإحراز (al-iḥrāz): Taking spoils into Dār al-Islām, which perfects the right but not ownership; it cuts off the share of latecomers.
السوقي (al-sūqī): A person who enters Dār al-Ḥarb for trade, not for fighting; he does not share in spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An army captures spoils in Dār al-Ḥarb. Before any iḥrāz, a group of volunteers arrives. According to the passage, do the volunteers share?
A) No, because volunteers are not regular soldiers.
B) Yes, because they joined before iḥrāz and are equal to other fighters.
C) Only if they actually fought.
D) No, because the spoils are already owned by the original soldiers.

Key Takeaway
Reinforcements share spoils only if they join before iḥrāz; the cause of entitlement is crossing the border, not actual fighting, so all participants share equally.

Prohibition of Selling Spoils Before Division
Defining the prohibition of sale before division and the imam's exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why selling spoils before division is haram for individual soldiers and under what conditions the imam may sell.

Core Idea
Spoils sale before division is haram for soldiers; imam may sell with ijtihād for maslaḥah.

This passage addresses the prohibition of selling spoils before division. For ordinary soldiers, the sale is haram because before iḥrāz they do not own the spoils, and after iḥrāz their share is unknown. However, the imam is permitted to sell spoils before division if he exercises ijtihād and finds a clear public benefit (maslaḥah), such as easing the burden of transporting spoils.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling spoils before division. The ruling for individual soldiers (ghuzāt) is haram.
2
Understand the reasoning
Before iḥrāz: no ownership. After iḥrāz: share unknown (jahālah). Both prevent a valid sale.
The prohibition is absolute for soldiers.
3
Distinguish the imam's position
The imam may sell with ijtihād based on maslaḥah. His authority allows him to sell even before division.
Al-Ṭaḥāwī validates it, provided the imam exercises ijtihād.
4
Identify the dalil
The text cites a hadith: 'al-nahy ‘an al-bay‘ qabl al-qisma' (prohibition of sale before division).
Not quoted verbatim, but referenced.
5
Note the condition for imam's sale
The imam must have a maslaḥah, e.g., reducing hardship of transport. The sale is not random but based on ijtihād.
No dislike (karāhah) attached to imam's sale when done correctly.

Key Terms
البيع قبل القسمة (al-bay‘ qabl al-qisma): Sale of spoils before formal division among eligible soldiers; prohibited for individuals, permissible for imam with ijtihād.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihād): Independent reasoning by a qualified scholar or ruler to derive a ruling in a new situation; here, it validates the imam's sale.
المصلحة (al-maslaḥah): Public benefit or interest that justifies exceptional rulings; in this case, alleviating hardship.

According to the passage, why is a soldier's sale of spoils before division haram?
A) Because it disrespects the imam's authority.

Key Takeaway
Soldiers' sale of spoils before division is haram due to lack of ownership or unknown share; the imam may sell with ijtihād for a valid maslaḥah.

Inheritance of Spoils and the Istihsan for Division Claims
Ruling on inheritance of spoils and istihsan for late claimants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a fighter's share in spoils is inherited after ihraz, and explain the istihsan exception to overturning a division.

Core Idea
A fighter's share becomes inheritable only after ihraz; a division is not overturned by a late claim, but compensation is given.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq introduces two key principles: the inheritance of shares in spoils, and the istihsan-based rule that once the imam has divided the spoils, a late claimant is compensated from the treasury rather than the division being overturned. We will analyze the legal reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage begins by stating that the share of a fighter is inherited, and fighters may use the spoils for certain needs without division. This establishes the basic rule that ownership and inheritance are tied to ihraz.
The basic rule: the share is inherited, and spoils can be used for fodder, food, etc. without formal division.
2
Locate the dalil for the division claim
The Tatarkhaniyya is quoted: if a claimant brings two witnesses after division, qiyas would overturn, but istihsan does not overturn and compensates from Bayt al-Mal.
The dalil is a transmitted ruling from the Tatarkhaniyya, not a primary text.
3
Analyze the istihsan
The division is valid and stability is preferred; the claimant's right is converted to monetary compensation. Istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid disruption.
Istihsan is a preferred juristic method in Hanafi school.
4
Note the cross-madhhab
Other schools may differ on overturning the division; Hanafis rely on istihsan to maintain stability.
The alternative qiyas would require overturning, which is problematic after distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
166 كتاب السير/ باب الغنائم وقسمتها يورث نصيبه وينتفع فيها بعلف وطعام وحطب وسلاح ودهن بلا قسمة ولا نبيعها التتارخانية : إذا قسم الإمام الغنيمة ثم جاء رجل وادعى أنه شهد الوقعة وأقام عدلين فالقياس أن ينقض القسمة. وفي الاستحسان لا ينقض ويعوض من بيت المال قيمة نصيبه اهـ قوله : (لا لسوقي (بلا (قتال أي لا شركة للسوقي في الغنيمة إذا لم يقاتل لا سهماً ولا رضخاً لأنه لم توجد المجاوزة على قصد القتال فانعدم السبب الظاهر فيعتبر السبب الحقيقي وهو القتال فيقيد الاستحقاق على حسب حاله فارساً أو راجلاً عند القتال. وأشار المصنف إلى أن الحربي إذا أسلم في دار الحرب أو المرتد إذا أسلم ولحق بالجيش لا يستحق شيئاً إن لم يقاتل، صرح به في المحيط. وذكر الشارح أن السوقي إذا قاتل ظهر أن قصده القتال والتجارة تبع له فلا يضره كالحاج إذا اتجر في طريق الحج لا ينقص أجره اهـ قوله : (ولا من مات فيها وبعد الإحراز بدارنا يورث (نصيبه لأن الإرث يجري في الملك ولا ملك قبل الإحراز وإنما الملك بعده كما قدمناه. وصرحوا في كتاب الوقف أن معلوم المستحق لا يورث بعد موته على أحد القولين، وفي قول يورث ولم أر ترجيحاً، وينبغي أن يفصل ؛ فإن كان مات بعد خروج وإحراز الناظر لها قبل القسمة يورث نصيب المستحق لتأكد الحق فيه فإن الغنيمة بعد الإحراز بدارنا يتأكد الحق فيها للغانمين ولا ملك لواحد بعينه في شيء قبل القسمة . أن النصيب يورث فكذا في الوظيفة، وإن مات قبل الإحراز في يد المتولى لا يورث نصيبه قياساً على مسألة الغنيمة، وسيأتي أن من مات من أهل الديوان قبل خروج العطاء لا يورث نصيبه، 6 الغلة قوله : (قياساً على مسألة (الغنيمة قال في النهر أقول في الدرر والغرر عن فوائد صاحب المحيط : للإمام والمؤذن وقف فلم يستوفيا حتى ماتا سقط لأنه في معنى الصلة، وكذا القاضي، وقيل: لا يسقط لأنه كالأجرة اهـ. وجزم في البغية بأنه يورث بخلاف رزق ،القاضي وأنت خبير بأن ما يأخذه القاضي ليس صلة كما هو ظاهر ولا أجراً لأن مثل هذه العبادة لم يقل أحد بجواز الاستئجار عليها بخلاف ما يأخذه الإمام والمؤذن فإنه لا ينفك عنهما، فبالنظر إلى الأجرة يورث ما يستحق إذا استحق غير مقيد بظهور الغلة وقبضها في يد الناظر وبالنظر إلى الصلة لا يورث وإن قبضه الناظر قبل الموت، وبهذا عرفت أن القياس على الغنيمة غير صحيح وسيأتي لهذا مزيد وبيان في الوقف إن شاء الله تعالى اهـ ما في النهر. ولم أر له في الوقف ذكراً لهذه المسألة، وكذا لم يذكرها المؤلف هناك أيضاً. هذا وقول النهر «إن ما يأخذه القاضي ليس صلة مخالف لما صرح به في الهداية قبيل الردة وسيذكره المؤلف هناك أيضاً. نعم ما يأخذه الإمام ونحوه فيه معنى الصلة ومعنى الأجرة، والظاهر أن ذلك منشأ الخلاف المحكي في الدرر لكن ما جزم به في البغية يقتضي ترجيح جانب الأجرة في حقه وهو ظاهر لا سيما على ما أفتى به المتأخرون من جواز الأجرة على الأذان والإمامة والتعليم. وعن والله تعالى أعلم مشى العلامة الطرسوسي على أن المدرس ونحوه إذا مات في أثناء السنة يعطى بقدر ما باشر ويسقط الباقي بخلاف الوقف على الأولاد والذرية فإنه إذا مات مستحق منهم يعتبر في حقه هذا اهـ. ثم اعلم أن من مات في دار الحرب إنما لا يورث نصيبه إذا مات قبل القسمة أو قبل البيع، أما إن مات بعد القسمة أو البيع في دار الحرب فإنه يورث نصيبه كما صرح به في التتارخانية
166 The Book of Siyar / Chapter on Spoils and Their Division. His share is inherited, and they may benefit from it in terms of fodder, food, firewood, weapons, and oil without division, and we do not sell it. Al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the Imam divides the spoils, then a man comes and claims that he witnessed the battle and brings two just witnesses, then by qiyas the division would be overturned. By istihsan, it is not overturned and he is compensated from the treasury with the value of his share. End. His saying: (Not for the market-goer) without fighting, meaning there is no partnership for the market-goer in the spoils if he did not fight, neither a share nor a radkh, because the crossing with the intention of fighting did not occur, so the apparent cause is absent, so the real cause, which is fighting, is considered, and entitlement is restricted according to his state as a horseman or foot soldier at the time of fighting. The author indicated that if a harbi becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb or an apostate becomes Muslim and joins the army, he is not entitled to anything if he did not fight, as stated in al-Muhit. The commentator mentioned that if the market-goer fought, it becomes apparent that his intention was fighting and trade is subsidiary to it, so it does not harm him, like the pilgrim who trades on the way to Hajj does not diminish his reward. End. His saying: (And not one who dies in it, and after ihraz in our land, his share is inherited) because inheritance occurs in ownership, and there is no ownership before ihraz; ownership is only after it, as we have mentioned. They explicitly stated in the Book of Waqf that the known stipend of the entitled person is not inherited after his death according to one of the two sayings, and in another saying it is inherited, and I have not seen a preference. It should be detailed: if he died after the issuance and ihraz by the administrator before division, the share of the entitled person is inherited because the right is confirmed in it, for the spoils after ihraz in our land, the right of the ghazis is confirmed in them, but there is no specific ownership for anyone in anything before division. So the share is inherited, likewise in the position. If he died before ihraz in the hand of the administrator, his share is not inherited, by qiyas on the issue of spoils. It will come that whoever among the people of the diwan dies before the distribution of the stipend, his share is not inherited. 6 Al-Ghalla. His saying: (By qiyas on the issue of spoils) He said in al-Nahr: I say in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar from the benefits of the author of al-Muhit: The imam and mu'adhdhin have a waqf, and they did not receive it until they died; it is forfeited because it is in the meaning of a gift, likewise the judge, and it is said: it is not forfeited because it is like wages. End. He affirmed in al-Bughya that it is inherited, unlike the stipend of the judge. And you are aware that what the judge takes is not a gift, as is apparent, nor wages, because no one has said that hiring is permissible for such an act of worship, unlike what the imam and mu'adhdhin take, for it is inseparable from them. With regard to wages, what is due is inherited if it is due not restricted by the appearance of the yield and its receipt in the hand of the administrator; with regard to gifts, it is not inherited even if the administrator received it before death. By this you know that the qiyas on the issue of spoils is not correct, and there will be more detail on this in waqf, if Allah wills. End of what is in al-Nahr. I have not seen any mention of this issue in waqf, nor did the author mention it there either. This, and the statement of al-Nahr that 'what the judge takes is not a gift' is contrary to what is stated in al-Hidayah before the chapter on apostasy, and the author will mention it there too. Yes, what the imam and the like take has the meaning of gift and the meaning of wages, and apparently that is the origin of the disagreement reported in al-Durar, but what is affirmed in al-Bughya necessitates preferring the aspect of wages in his case, which is apparent, especially according to what later scholars issued fatwas on, of the permissibility of wages for adhan, imamah, and teaching. And from Allah, the Exalted, is knowledge. Allama al-Tarsusi followed that the teacher and the like, if he dies during the year, is given according to what he performed, and the remainder is forfeited, unlike the waqf for children and offspring, for if an entitled person among them dies, it is considered in his case. This ends. Then know that whoever dies in Dar al-Harb, his share is not inherited if he dies before division or before sale. But if he dies after division or sale in Dar al-Harb, his share is inherited, as stated in al-Tatarkhaniyya.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing several rulings related to the inheritance of shares in spoils (ghanima). The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains each part of the matn's statement. The first ruling: if the imam divides the spoils and then someone claims he was present at the battle with two witnesses, the division is not overturned by istihsan (juristic preference) but he is compensated from the treasury. This is based on the principle that the division was valid and should not be disrupted, but the claimant's right is preserved via compensation. Second: the market-goer (souqi) who does not fight gets no share, because the real cause of entitlement is fighting. If he fights, trade is subsidiary and does not affect his entitlement, like a pilgrim who trades. Third: a fighter who dies before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam (before ihraz) does not have his share inherited because ownership only occurs after ihraz. If he dies after ihraz (even before division), his share is inherited. The commentator then compares this with waqf stipends: there is a difference of opinion whether the stipend of an imam or mu'adhdhin is inherited. Some say it is like a gift and not inherited, others say it is like wages and thus inherited. The preferred view is that it is inherited, like wages, especially in later fatwas. The passage ends by clarifying that dying in Dar al-Harb before division or sale prevents inheritance, but after division or sale, the share is inherited. The commentary consistently uses qiyas (analogy) and istihsan to derive rulings, showing the Hanafi method.

Key Terms
الإحراز (al-ihraz): Bringing the spoils of war to a safe place in Dar al-Islam, at which point the fighters' ownership becomes established.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference, where a ruling is derived by setting aside strict analogy in favor of a more suitable ruling based on broader objectives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a claimant with two witnesses appears after the imam has divided the spoils?
A) The division is overturned and the spoils are redistributed.
B) The division stands and the claimant is compensated from the treasury.
C) The claimant is given a share from the next spoils.
D) The claimant's witnesses are rejected because the division is final.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to preserve the validity of a completed division, compensating the late claimant from the treasury.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
6 min
The Market-Goer (Souqi) and Entitlement to Spoils
Ruling on market-goer's entitlement to spoils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a market-goer who does not fight receives no share of spoils, and identify the exception if he fights.

Core Idea
A market-goer (souqi) gets no share unless he actually fights, because fighting is the real cause of entitlement.

This passage clarifies the status of a trader who accompanies the army: if he does not fight, he receives no share, but if he fights, his trade is considered secondary and he is entitled. The analogy to a pilgrim who trades is given to show that a secondary purpose does not undermine the primary intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
The passage discusses the 'souqi' – a market-goer or trader who accompanies the army without intending to fight.
The souqi is distinct from a fighter or a volunteer.
2
State the default ruling
If the souqi does not fight, he gets no share (neither a full share nor a radkh) because the cause of entitlement – fighting – is absent.
The apparent cause (crossing with the army) is not enough; the real cause is fighting.
3
Identify the exception
If the souqi actually fights, his primary intention is considered fighting, and trade is subsidiary. He is then entitled as a fighter.
The analogy of a pilgrim trading on Hajj is used: his reward is not diminished.
4
Apply to similar cases
The author extends this to a harbi who becomes Muslim or an apostate who returns to Islam and joins the army: if they do not fight, they get nothing.
The ruling is consistent: fighting is the decisive factor.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing several rulings related to the inheritance of shares in spoils (ghanima). The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains each part of the matn's statement. The first ruling: if the imam divides the spoils and then someone claims he was present at the battle with two witnesses, the division is not overturned by istihsan (juristic preference) but he is compensated from the treasury. This is based on the principle that the division was valid and should not be disrupted, but the claimant's right is preserved via compensation. Second: the market-goer (souqi) who does not fight gets no share, because the real cause of entitlement is fighting. If he fights, trade is subsidiary and does not affect his entitlement, like a pilgrim who trades. Third: a fighter who dies before the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam (before ihraz) does not have his share inherited because ownership only occurs after ihraz. If he dies after ihraz (even before division), his share is inherited. The commentator then compares this with waqf stipends: there is a difference of opinion whether the stipend of an imam or mu'adhdhin is inherited. Some say it is like a gift and not inherited, others say it is like wages and thus inherited. The preferred view is that it is inherited, like wages, especially in later fatwas. The passage ends by clarifying that dying in Dar al-Harb before division or sale prevents inheritance, but after division or sale, the share is inherited. The commentary consistently uses qiyas (analogy) and istihsan to derive rulings, showing the Hanafi method.

Key Terms
السوقي (al-souqi): A market-goer or trader who accompanies the army without intending to fight.
الرضخ (al-radkh): A smaller discretionary share given to non-combatants like women, children, and slaves if they participate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a market-goer (souqi) become entitled to a share of the spoils?
A) Always, because he accompanied the army.
B) Only if the imam gives him permission.
C) Only if he actually fights.
D) Only if he is a horseman.

Key Takeaway
Entitlement to spoils requires actual fighting; mere accompaniment or trade is insufficient.

Inheritance After Ihraz and the Khilaf on Waqf Stipends
Ruling on inheritance after ihraz and khilaf on waqf stipends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on inheritance of spoils after ihraz and compare it with the khilaf on inheritance of waqf stipends.

Core Idea
A fighter's share is inherited after ihraz, but waqf stipends are debated: some treat them as gifts (not inherited), others as wages (inherited).

This passage details the inheritance of a fighter's share after the spoils are brought to Dar al-Islam (ihraz). It then extends the discussion to waqf stipends: whether the stipend of an imam, mu'adhdhin, or teacher is inherited after death. The commentator introduces a khilaf and eventually prefers the view that stipends are inherited as wages.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for spoils
If a fighter dies after ihraz (spoils in Dar al-Islam), his share is inherited because ownership is established. If he dies before ihraz, there is no inheritance.
Ihraz is the key condition for ownership.
2
Contrast with waqf stipends
The passage then moves to waqf stipends for positions like imam and mu'adhdhin. There is a known khilaf: some say the stipend is not inherited (like a gift), others say it is inherited (like wages).
The commentator notes he has not seen a clear tarjih.
3
Analyze the detailed view
The preferred view is to differentiate: if the beneficiary dies after the stipend has been 'issued and ihraz' by the administrator (i.e., allocated), it is inherited; if before, it is not. This parallels the spoils rule.
The term 'ihraz' is used for the stipend as well, meaning the administrator has set it aside.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator eventually supports the view that stipends are inherited, especially for imams and mu'adhdhins, based on later fatwas that permit wages for these roles. The stipend is akin to wages.
Al-Bughya affirms inheritance for imam/mu'adhdhin but not for qadi's salary.
