Imam's Authority to Grant Anfal as Incentive
Ruling on imam granting anfal with intra-Hanafi detail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on anfal and distinguish between valid and invalid forms of anfal based on the source text.

Core Idea
Anfal is a recommended incentive, but granting all booty to a sariyah is valid only from Dar al-Harb, not Dar al-Islam.

The imam has the authority to grant extra spoils (anfal) to fighters as a means of incitement. This lesson examines the ruling, its basis in the Quran, and a key intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the imam can grant all the booty to a raiding party (sariyah). You will learn the conditions that make anfal valid and the distinction between general and specific grants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
The matn states that the imam may grant anfal by promising a fighter the spoil of his slain enemy, or by promising a sariyah a portion after khums. Note that anfal is a recommended (mandub) act of incitement, not obligatory.
The author prefers 'recommended' over 'no harm' because it aligns with the Quranic command to incite.
2
Understand the proof (Quran 8:65)
The verse commands incitement of believers for battle, and anfal is one form of incitement. The command is general, so anfal is a recommended method, not an obligation.
The dalal of the verse is zanni; it supports the ruling but does not make anfal fard or wajib.
3
Distinguish general vs specific anfal
The text explains that if the imam grants all booty to the whole army, it is invalid because it nullifies the obligatory shares (like the army's portions). But grant to a sariyah (a detachment) may be valid if it does not negate the rights of others.
General anfal abolishes shares; specific anfal to a subgroup for encouragement is permissible with conditions.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Hidayah says granting all booty to a sariyah is valid. Al-Sarakhsi in al-Siyar al-Kabir adds a condition: the sariyah must be sent from within Dar al-Harb, not from Dar al-Islam. The mufta bihi follows al-Sarakhsi's detail.
The difference hinges on whether the sariyah already has a prior claim to the booty before anfal.
5
Apply the outcome
The ruling is that anfal is valid if it does not abolish obligatory shares. For a sariyah from Dar al-Islam, granting all is invalid; from Dar al-Harb, it is valid as an incentive.
This preserves the system of spoils distribution while allowing flexibility for tactical encouragement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وللإمام أن ينفل بقوله من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه وبقوله للسرية جعلت لكم الربع بعد الخمس وينفل أي بعدما دفع الخمس للفقراء لأن التحريض مندوب إليه قال الله تعالى يا أيها النبي حرض المؤمنين على القتال) [الأنفال : ٦٥] وهذا نوع تحريض فلو قال المصنف ويستحب للإمام لكان أولى. وقول من قال لا بأس للإمام لا يخالفه لأنها تستعمل في المندوب أيضاً كما تقدم في الجنائز فلم تكن مضطردة لما تركه أولى . ثم قد يكون التنفيل بما ذكر وقد يكون بغيره كالدراهم والدنانير أو يقول من أخذ شيئاً فهو له، فما ذكر في المختصر مثال لا قيد لكن قالوا لو قال للعسكر كلما أخذتم فهو لكم بالسوية بعد الخمس أو للسرية لم يجز لأن فيه إبطال السهمان الذي أوجبها لشرع إذ فيه لكنه لا ينحصر في التنفيل ليكون التنفيل واجباً بل يكون بغيره أيضاً من الموعظة الحسنة والترغيب فيما عند الله تعالى، فإذا كان التنفيل أحد خصال التحريض كان التنفيل واجباً مخيراً. ثم إذا كان هو ادعى الخصال إلى المقصود يكون إسقاط الواجب به دون غيره مما يسقط به أولى وهو المندوب فصار المندوب اختيار الإسقاط به دون غيره لا هو في نفسه بل هو واجب مخير، وأما ما قيل في التنفيل البعض وتوهين آخرين وتوهين المسلم حرام فليس بشيء وإلا حرم التنفيل لاستلزامه محرماً ترجیح مع اهـ. قوله : (أو للسرية) عطف على قوله للعسكر لكن هذا مخالف لما في الهداية حيث فرق بين العسكر والسرية فقال : ولا ينبغي للإمام أن ينفل بكل المأخوذ لأن فيه إبطال حق الكل وإن فعله السرية جاز لأن التصرف إليه وقد تكون المصلحة فيه .اهـ وكذا قال الزيلعي أنه لو نفل السرية بالكل جاز، وذكر في الاختيار كما في الهداية ونقل في الدرر عن النهاية عن السير الكبير نحوه . قلت : لكن الذي رأيته في السير الكبير للسرخسي التفصيل في السرية فإنه قال : لو بعث أمير المصيصة سرية لا ينبغي أن ينفل لهم ما أصابوا بخلاف ما إذا دخل الإمام مع الجيش في دار الحرب ثم بعث سرية ونفل لهم ما أصابوا فإنه يجوز لأن السرية في الأول يختصون بما أصابوا قبل تنفيل الإمام وليس لأهل المصيصة معهم شركة في ذلك فإن المصيصة من دار الإسلام ومن توطن في دار الإسلام لا يشارك الجيش فيما أصابوا فليس في هذا التنفيل إلا إبطال الخمس وفي الثاني لا يختصون بالمصاب قبل التنفيل فهذا تنفيل للتخصيص على وجه التحريض فيصح .اهـ. وحاصله أنه إن بعث السرية من دار الإسلام لم يكن له التنفيل بكل ما أصابوا لأنهم صاروا بمنزلة الجيش من العسكر لأنهم كل العسكر بخلاف ما إذا بعث السرية من دار الحرب لأنهم قطعة من العسكر خصهم بما أصابوا للتحريض، وهذا شأن التنفيل من زيادة البعض على غيرهم للتحريض كما بين ذلك بعد نحو ورقة بقوله : ولو بعث السرية من دار الإسلام ونفلهم الثلث بعد الخمس أو قبل الخمس كان باطلاً لأنه ما خص بعضهم بالتنفيل وليس مقصوده فيه إلا إبطال الخمس وإبطال تفضيل الفارس على الراجل فلا يجوز بخلاف ما إذا التقوا في دار الحرب ففي التنفيل هناك معنى التخصيص لهم لأن الجيش شركاؤهم في الغنيمة ففي التنفيل تخصيصهم ببعض المصاب وهو مستقيم اهـ. وحاصله أن التنفيل العام لا يصح وذلك في العسكر وفي السرية المبعوثة من دارنا لأنها بمنزلة العسكر. ووجه بطلانه أنه
His statement: (And for the imam to grant anfal by saying: Whoever kills an enemy, his spoil is his, and by saying to the sariyah: I have given you one-fourth after the khums.) He grants anfal after paying the khums to the poor, because incitement is recommended; Allah said: 'O Prophet, incite the believers to fight' (8:65), and this is a type of incitement. If the author said 'it is recommended for the imam' it would be better. The one who said 'there is no harm for the imam' does not contradict because it is used for the recommended as well, as in funerals. Then anfal may be with what was mentioned or with other things like dirhams and dinars, or he says: Whoever takes something, it is his. What was mentioned in the Mukhtasar is an example, not a condition. But they said: If he says to the army, 'Whatever you take is yours equally after the khums,' or to the sariyah, it is not valid because it nullifies the shares that the Law has made obligatory. But it is not confined to anfal to make anfal obligatory; rather, it is also done by other means like good advice and encouraging what is with Allah. So if anfal is one of the means of incitement, it becomes obligatory by choice. Then if anfal is the best means to achieve the goal, dropping the obligation with it is better, thus it becomes recommended. What is said that anfal to some and weakening others is forbidden is invalid, otherwise anfal would be forbidden because it entails something haram. His statement: (or to the sariyah) is connected to his statement 'to the army', but this contradicts what is in al-Hidayah which distinguishes between the army and sariyah: The imam should not grant anfal of all booty because it invalidates the right of all, but if he does so for a sariyah, it is valid because disposal is to it and there may be benefit. Al-Zayla‘i also said that if he grants anfal of all to a sariyah, it is valid. In al-Ikhtiyar it is like al-Hidayah. But I saw in al-Siyar al-Kabir of al-Sarakhsi a detail: If the amir of al-Massisah sends a sariyah, he should not grant them what they seize, unlike when the imam enters Dar al-Harb with the army and then sends a sariyah and grants them what they seize, which is valid. Because in the first, the sariyah already have a specific claim before the imam's anfal, and the people of al-Massisah do not share with them since it is Dar al-Islam, so the anfal only nullifies the khums. In the second, they do not have a specific claim before anfal, so it is a valid anfal for encouragement. Summary: If the sariyah is sent from Dar al-Islam, he cannot grant all what they seize because they become like the army. If from Dar al-Harb, it is valid because they are a portion of the army, so it is a specific incentive. This is the general rule: general anfal is invalid for the army and for sariyah from our land, because they are like the army. The reason for its invalidity is...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the imam's power to grant anfal (extra spoils) as an incentive. The matn states the imam can promise a fighter the spoil of his slain enemy, or promise a raiding party (sariyah) one-fourth after khums. The commentary explains that this is a form of incitement (tahrid) recommended by the Quran (8:65). Some scholars prefer the word 'recommended' over 'no harm' because anfal is not obligatory. The main debate is whether the imam can grant all the booty to a sariyah. Al-Hidayah distinguishes: granting all the booty to the whole army is invalid because it abolishes the shares of others, but to a sariyah (smaller detachment) it may be valid. However, al-Sarakhsi in al-Siyar al-Kabir gives a detailed condition: if the sariyah is sent from Dar al-Islam, they are like the army (their territory is not at war), so granting all invalidates the shares; but if sent from within Dar al-Harb (while the imam is present), the sariyah does not already have a claim before anfal, so granting all is valid incentive. This resolves the apparent contradiction. The general principle: anfal that is general (to all) is invalid; specific anfal to a portion for encouragement is valid if it does not invalidate prior rights.

Key Terms
تنفيل (tanfil): The imam's grant of extra spoils (anfal) to fighters as an incentive, typically from the khums or booty.
سرية (sariyah): A military detachment sent by the imam or commander on a mission, smaller than the main army.
تحريض (tahrid): Incitement to fight, recommended in the Quran (8:65).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Sarakhsi in al-Siyar al-Kabir, when is it valid for the imam to grant all booty to a sariyah?
A) When the sariyah is sent from Dar al-Islam
B) When the sariyah is sent from within Dar al-Harb while the imam is with the army
C) When the imam declares a general amnesty
D) When the sariyah consists of only horsemen

Key Takeaway
Anfal is a recommended incentive, but granting all booty to a sariyah is valid only if the sariyah is sent from within Dar al-Harb, not from Dar al-Islam.

Joint Killing and Sharing of Salab: The Mubariz Condition
Ruling on sharing salab with condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint killing of a harbi, identify the condition that the victim must be a mubariz, and apply the istihsan argument to determine when sharing of salab is valid.

Core Idea
Salab is shared only when the victim is a mubariz — a condition justified by istihsan to prevent abuse.

This lesson examines a key rule in the laws of spoils: when two fighters jointly kill an enemy, do they both get his personal belongings? The answer is not simply 'yes' – it depends on whether the victim was a capable warrior. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to restrict the literal analogy, ensuring that salab is not trivialized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The default rule: if two men share in killing a harbi, they share his salab. The author states this unconditionally, then immediately introduces a qualification.
2
Locate the condition
The qualification from Sharh al-Tahawi: the killed must be a mubariz – a warrior who could resist each killer individually. If he is weak, the salab becomes general spoils.
Mubariz means 'champion' or 'one who can fight back'.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
The author notes that by qiyas (analogy), even three or more killers would share because 'whoever' is general, but this leads to absurdity (the whole army sharing one salab). Istihsan restricts sharing to cases where the victim could have defended himself against the killers.
Istihsan here is based on the apparent custom ('urf) that such a victim would have been able to fight back.
4
Apply to further cases
The text also covers: if the Imam addresses only one, that one gets the salab even if another assists; if two are killed together, the killer chooses one salab; and who qualifies for salab (any fighter entitled to a share or radhkh, including dhimmis, women, etc.).
These sub-rules flow from the same condition of mubariz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب الغنائم وقسمتها
وإذا اشترك رجلان في قتل حربي اشتركا في سلبه. وقيده في شرح الطحاوي بأن يكون المقتول مبارزاً يقاوم الكل، فإن كان عاجزاً لا يستحقون سلبه ويكون غنيمة، وإن قيده الإمام بقوله وحده لا يستحقان سلبه، ولو كان الخطاب لواحد فشاركه آخر استحق المخاطب وحده، ولو خاطب واحداً فقتل المخاطب رجلين فله سلب الأول خاصة إلا إذا قتلهما معا فله واحد. والخيار في تعيينه للمقاتل لا للإمام، ولو كان على العموم فقتل رجل اثنين فأكثر استحق سلبهما ويستحق السلب من يستحق السهم أو الرضخ فيشتمل الذمي والتاجر والمرأة والعبد، ولا بد أن يكون المقتول منهم مباح القتل حتى لا يستحق السلب بقتل النساء والمجانين والصبيان الذين لم يقاتلوا، ولا يشترط في استحقاق السلب سماع القاتل مقالة الإمام حتى لو قتل من لم يسمع فله السلب لأنه ليس في وسع الإمام إسماع الأفراد وإنما في وسعه إشاعة الخطاب وقد وجد.
قوله : (وإذا اشترك رجلان (الخ قيد بهما لأنه لو كانوا ثلاثة أو أكثر فالقياس كذلك لأن «من» للعموم ولكنه قبيح لأنه يؤدي إلى أنه لو اجتمع العسكر كلهم على قتله فلهم سلبه وليس مراده ذلك، والاستحسان يحتمل وجوهاً أحسنها أنه إن قتله قوم يرى الناس أن ذلك القتيل لو خلى بينه وبينهم كان ينتصف منهم فلهم سلبه وإلا فلا وتمامه في شرح السير الكبير
Book of Siyar / Chapter of Spoils and Their Division. And if two men share in killing a harbi (enemy combatant), they share in his salab (personal belongings). And it is restricted in Sharh al-Tahawi to the condition that the killed be a mubariz (champion) who can resist all, for if he is weak, they do not deserve his salab and it becomes ghanima (spoils). And if the Imam restricts it by his statement, they do not deserve his salab together. And if the address was to one and another joins him, the addressed one alone deserves. And if he addresses one and the addressed one kills two men, he gets the salab of the first specifically unless he killed them both together, then he gets one (choice). The choice of determination is for the fighter, not for the Imam. And if it was general and a man kills two or more, he deserves their salab. And the one who deserves the salab is the one who deserves the share (sahm) or the radhkh (small grant), which includes the dhimmi, the merchant, the woman, and the slave. And it is necessary that the killed among them be one whose killing is permissible, so that salab is not deserved by killing women, insane persons, and boys who do not fight. And it is not a condition for deserving salab that the killer hear the speech of the Imam, so even if he kills one who did not hear, he still has the salab because it is not within the capacity of the Imam to make individuals hear; rather, it is within his capacity to broadcast the address, and that has occurred. His statement: (and if two men share... etc.) He restricted it to two because if there were three or more, the analogy is likewise because 'whoever' is general, but it is ugly because it would lead to that if the entire army gathered on killing him, they would have his salab, and that is not his intention. Istihsan (juristic preference) has several aspects; the best is that if a group kills him and people see that that killed person, if left between them, would have defended himself against them, they have his salab; otherwise not. And its completion is in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the situation when two persons jointly kill an enemy combatant. The default ruling is that they share the salab (the personal belongings of the killed). However, the author qualifies this: the killed must be a mubariz, meaning a valiant warrior capable of defending himself against each of them singly. If the killed is weak or helpless, the killers do not get his salab; it becomes part of the general spoils. The text further discusses cases where the Imam specifically addresses one person to kill; then only that person gets the salab, even if another assists. If the address is general, the killer of two gets both salabs. The last part of the passage provides the reasoning: analogically, even three or more would share, but that is rejected because it would mean a whole army could share one salab. Instead, istihsan restricts the sharing to those who could have been resisted by the victim, justifying the division.

Key Terms
سلب (salab): The personal belongings of a slain enemy combatant, including his weapons, mount, and clothes, which become the property of the killer(s).
مبارز (mubariz): A valiant warrior who can fight and defend himself against an opponent; the text uses it to define who qualifies as a victim for salab sharing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two soldiers jointly kill an enemy combatant. Under what condition do they share his salab according to the Hanafi school?
A) In all cases of joint killing.
B) Only if the killed was a mubariz capable of resisting each individually.
C) Only if the Imam gave prior permission.
D) Only if they killed him during the day.

Key Takeaway
Joint killers share salab only when the victim was a mubariz; otherwise it becomes general spoils.

Nafal: Duration and Conditions for Validity
Rulings on duration of nafal and conditions for armor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration of a nafal offer for killing, identify when nafal for entering with armor is valid, and apply the condition of benefit (manfa'ah) to distinguish valid from invalid nafal incentives.

Core Idea
Nafal is valid only when it encourages actions that bring clear benefit to the Muslim army.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq that expands on the rules of nafal—extra incentives given by the Imam in jihad. The passage clarifies that a nafal offer for killing lasts for the entire campaign unless rescinded, and that nafal for entering with equipment is allowed only when it provides benefit to the Muslims. Understanding these conditions prevents misuse of incentives and ensures they serve the common good.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of nafal discussed
The passage covers nafal for killing (taking the slain's salab) and nafal for entering Dar al-Harb with specific equipment (shields, horse, spears, bows). Recognize that each category has distinct rules.
2
Analyze the duration rule for nafal on killing
The nafal applies to every battle in that journey until the fighters return. It remains valid even if the original ruler dies or is replaced, as long as the new ruler does not rescind it. If the Imam specifies a particular time (e.g., 'during this battle'), that restriction holds.
This shows durability of the Imam's offer.
3
Examine the conditions for nafal on entering with shields
Nafal for entering with one or two shields is permissible. For more than two, it is only permissible if there is benefit (manfa'ah) to the Muslims. This introduces the key condition: benefit to the community.
4
Understand the prohibition for horse and the analogy for spears/bows
Nafal for entering with a horse is not permitted. However, spears and bows are treated like shields (permissible) because they provide defensive/offensive utility. The distinction is based on the presence or absence of clear benefit.
The underlying illah is benefit.
5
Derive the general principle
From the cases, we extract the Hanafi rule: a nafal offer is valid if it motivates an action that brings tangible benefit to the Muslim army. The Imam must assess benefit before announcing such incentives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه يقع على كل قتال في تلك السفر ما لم يرجعوا وإن مات الوالي أو عزل ما لم يمنعه الثاني. وإن قال حالة القتال يتعين ذلك، ولو قال من دخل دار الحرب بدرع فله كذا جاز، وكذا بدرعين. ولا يجوز ما زاد إلا إذا كان فيه منفعة للمسلمين بخلاف ما إذا قال من دخل بفرس كذا فإنه لا يجوز والرماح والأقواس كالدرع
And in al-TatarKhaniyya: Whoever kills a slain person, he has his salab; it applies to every battle in that journey as long as they have not returned, even if the ruler dies or is dismissed, as long as the second (ruler) does not forbid it. And if he says (during) the state of fighting, it is determined by that. And if he says: Whoever enters Dar al-Harb with a shield (dir'), he gets such-and-such, it is permissible, and likewise with two shields. And more than that is not permissible unless there is benefit for the Muslims, contrary to if he says: Whoever enters with a horse such-and-such, for that is not permissible. And spears and bows are like the shield.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage expands on the nafal (extra incentive) given by the Imam. It first states that a general nafal offer for killing applies to all battles of that campaign until the fighters return, even if the ruler changes. If the Imam specifies a particular time of fighting, that restriction applies. Then it discusses nafal for entering battle with a shield: giving extra for one or two shields is valid, but for more than two only if there is a clear benefit for Muslims. However, giving nafal for entering with a horse is not valid because it does not provide a similar advantage. Spears and bows are analogized to shields. This shows that the permissibility is based on actual benefit (manfa'ah) to the Muslim army, not merely on the action.

Key Terms
نفل (nafal): An extra grant or incentive given by the Imam to fighters beyond their regular share of spoils, to encourage specific actions.
درع (dir'): Shield or armor; the text uses it as an example of equipment that provides defensive benefit to Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is nafal for entering with a horse not permissible according to this passage?
A) Because horses are not allowed for warfare.
B) Because there is no benefit (manfa'ah) for Muslims in that action.
C) Because horses are too valuable.
D) Because the Imam did not mention horses.

Key Takeaway
A nafal offer is valid for the whole campaign until the fighters return and is conditioned on benefit; nafal for entering with equipment is allowed for shields but not horses, unless benefit exists.

Authority of the Sariya Leader to Grant Nafal
Rulings on when a sariya leader can grant nafal and its source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a sariya leader may grant nafal and identify the valid source of such nafal according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A sariya leader's nafal is valid only from the sariya's own share, unless the sariya returns before the main army joins.

When a military detachment (sariya) operates separately from the main army, the leader's authority to grant extra spoils (nafal) is carefully regulated. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the limitations: the Imam's orders, the soldiers' consent, and the nature of the partnership between the sariya and the main army determine the validity and source of nafal. Understanding these rules ensures that the distribution of spoils remains just and within the bounds of Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage rules on the validity of a sariya leader granting nafal. First, determine the general principle: the leader's authority is derivative from the Imam.
The sariya leader is not an independent commander; his power is delegated.
2
Analyze the condition of Imam's prohibition
If the Imam explicitly forbids nafal, the leader cannot grant it unless his soldiers consent. If they consent, nafal is valid from the four-fifths (the soldiers' share after khums). If the Imam did not forbid, the leader acts in the Imam's place.
The soldiers' consent overrides the Imam's prohibition for their own share.
3
Examine the scenario of additional nafal
The passage presents a case: the Imam grants a nafal of one-third to the sariya, then the leader gives extra nafal for specific acts (e.g., conquering a fortress). The validity depends on the source: from the sariya's share it is valid; from the main army's share it is only valid if the sariya returns to Dar al-Islam before the main army joins them.
Partnership (shirka) between sariya and main army determines the share source.
4
Understand the effect of independence
If the sariya returns before the main army joins, there is no partnership, so the leader's nafal covers all spoils. The main army's leader's nafal becomes void in that case.
The sariya becomes an independent unit upon return before joining.
5
Note the discretion on unspecified nafal
The text concludes that nafal can be granted even if the amount is unspecified (e.g., 'a portion' or 'a little'). The leader has discretion to determine the amount, but it must be less than half.
Uncertainty in the amount does not invalidate nafal; the leader's ijtihad applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد المصنف بالإمام لأنه أمير السرية إذ نهاه الإمام عن التنفيل فليس له أن ينفل إلا إذا رضي العسكر بنفله فيجوز من أربعة الأخماس وإن لم ينهه له ذلك لأنه قائم مقام الإمام. ولو نفل الإمام السرية بالثلث بعد الخمس ثم إن أميرها نفل لفتح الحصن أو للمبارزة بغير أمر الإمام، فإن نفل من حصة السرية يجوز، ولا يجوز من سهام العسكر إلا إذا رجعت السرية إلى دار الإسلام قبل لحاق العسكر، فإن نفل أميرهم جائز من جميع ما أصابوا لأنه لا شركة للعسكر معهم فجاز نفل أمير السرية وبطل نفل أمير العسكر. ولا فرق في النفل بين أن يكون معلوماً أو مجهولاً، فلو قال من جاء منكم بشيء فله منه طائفة فجاء رجل بمتاع وآخر بثياب وآخر برؤوس فالرأي للأمير ولو قال له منه قليل أو أو شيء أعطاه أقل من النصف والجزء النصف وما دونه وسهم رجل من القوم يعطيه يسير
And the author restricted (it) to the Imam because he is the leader of the sariya. If the Imam forbade him from giving nafal, he cannot give nafal unless the soldiers agree to his nafal; then it is permissible from the four-fifths. And if he did not forbid him, he may do so because he stands in the place of the Imam. And if the Imam gave nafal to the sariya of one-third after the khums, then its leader gave nafal for the conquest of a fortress or for a duel without the Imam's order, then if he gave from the sariya's share, it is permissible; it is not permissible from the shares of the main army unless the sariya returns to Dar al-Islam before the main army joins them. Then the nafal of their leader is permissible from all they acquired because there is no partnership with the main army, so the nafal of the sariya leader is valid and the nafal of the main army leader is void. And there is no difference in nafal whether it is known or unknown. So if he says: Whoever among you brings something, he gets a portion of it, and a man brings goods, another clothes, another heads (slaves), then the opinion is for the leader. And if he says: from it a little or something, he gives less than half; and the portion is half or less; and a share of a man from the people, he gives a little.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage discusses the authority of the leader of a small detachment (sariya) to grant nafal. If the Imam has forbidden nafal, the leader cannot give it without the consent of his soldiers; if consent is given, it is permissible from the four-fifths (the soldiers' share after khums). If the Imam did not forbid, the leader stands in his place. The text then examines a scenario: the Imam gives a nafal of one-third to the sariya, and then the sariya leader gives additional nafal for specific achievements. That nafal is valid only from the sariya's own share, not from the main army's share, unless the sariya returns to Islamic territory before the main army joins, in which case they are independent and the leader's nafal covers all spoils. The last part explains that the amount of nafal can be determined by the leader's discretion even if unspecified.

Key Terms
أمير السرية (amir al-sariya): The leader of a military detachment (sariya) sent by the Imam for a specific mission.
شركة (shirka): Partnership; here it refers to the legal partnership between the sariya and the main army in the spoils before they separate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a sariya leader's nafal from the main army's shares be valid?
A) Always, if the leader agrees.
B) Only if the sariya returns to Dar al-Islam before the main army joins them.
C) Only if the Imam permits.
D) Never, because the sariya leader has no authority over the main army.

Key Takeaway
A sariya leader's nafal is restricted by the Imam's orders and the partnership with the main army; it is valid only from the sariya's share unless the sariya returns before the main army joins, making them independent.

Definition of Tanfil and Conditional Nafal Rules
Definition of tanfil and examples of conditional nafal offers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that nafal after ihraz is restricted to the khums and apply the distinction between valid and invalid conditional nafal promises.

Core Idea
After spoils are secured (ihraz), the Imam can only grant nafal from the khums, not from the fighters' shares.

The term 'tanfil' (granting extra spoils to a fighter) is a special incentive in jihad. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, we learn the critical condition that after the spoils are brought under Muslim control (ihraz), the Imam may only give such extra grants from the one-fifth (khums). The passage also clarifies the fate of the killed enemy's personal belongings (salab) and illustrates how conditional promises must be interpreted strictly. These rules prevent unfairness among fighters and ensure the spoils are distributed according to the Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its restriction
Locate the phrase 'بعد الإحراز من الخمس فقط'. This tells us that nafal is only permissible from the khums after the spoils have been secured. Understand that the four-fifths belong to the fighters and cannot be used for extra grants.
The timing (after ihraz) and source (khums) are both essential conditions.
2
Analyse the salab rule
Note that the salab (mount, clothes, weapons) of a killed enemy belongs to the killer automatically unless the Imam explicitly grants additional nafal. This is the default rule.
Salab is not from the khums; it's a separate entitlement of the killer.
3
Examine conditional nafal examples
Consider the two examples: (1) 'Whoever brings a thousand gets two thousand' – the fighter gets only one thousand because the condition was on bringing, not on doubling. (2) 'Whoever brings a captive gets the captive and a thousand dirhams' – the fighter gets both, because each item is explicitly promised.
The promise must be grammatically and logically clear; ambiguity is resolved against the fighter.
4
Define tanfil linguistically and legally
Understand that tanfil is derived from 'nafl' meaning extra. Legally, it is the Imam giving a fighter (especially a horseman) more than his regular share. The term also applies to grandchildren and to supererogatory acts.
The two pronunciations (tanfil and nafal) are both valid Arabic dialects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد الإحراز من الخمس فقط والسلب للكل إن لم ينفل وهو مركبه وثيابه وسلاحه وما معه. سهم الراجل، ولو قال من جاء بألف فله ألفان فجاء بألف لا يعطى إلا ألف، ولو قال من جاء بالأسير فله الأسير وألف درهم فإنه يعطى ذلك، والفرق وتمام التفريعات في المحيط . والتنفيل إعطاء الإمام الفارس فوق سهمه وهو من النفل وهو الزائد ومنه النافلة الزائد على الفرض، ويقال لولد الولد كذلك أيضاً ويقال نفله تنفيلاً ونفله بالتخفيف نفلاً لغتان فصيحتان.
After ihraz (taking control of spoils), (nafal is) from the khums only. And the salab is for everyone if he (the Imam) did not grant (explicitly) nafal, and it is his mount, clothes, weapons, and what is with him. The share of the foot soldier. And if he says: Whoever brings a thousand, he gets two thousand, and he brings a thousand, he is given only one thousand. And if he says: Whoever brings a captive, he gets the captive and a thousand dirhams, he is given that. The difference and complete subdivisions are in al-Muhit. And al-tanfil is the Imam giving the horseman more than his share; it is from al-nafl, which is the extra, and from it is al-nafila, the extra beyond the obligatory. It is also used for the child of a child. And it is said: nafalahu tanfilan and nafalahu with tashdid and takhfif, nafalan, two eloquent dialects.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage begins with a key ruling: after the spoils have been taken and secured (ihraz), nafal can only be given from the khums (one-fifth), not from the four-fifths that belong to the fighters. The salab (personal belongings of the killed) is for the killer without any nafal unless explicitly stated. Then it gives examples of conditional nafal: if the Imam says 'whoever brings a thousand gets two thousand', but the fighter brings a thousand, he gets only one thousand (the promise of double was conditional on bringing, not on the amount). If he says 'whoever brings a captive gets the captive and a thousand dirhams', he gets both. The details are in al-Muhit. Finally, it defines tanfil linguistically: it is giving a horseman extra beyond his share, and it is derived from the root nafala meaning increase. The term can also refer to a grandchild. The word has two pronunciations.

Key Terms
تنفيل (tanfil): The act of the Imam giving a fighter an additional grant beyond his regular share of spoils.
إحراز (ihraz): The act of taking possession and securing the spoils; after ihraz, the spoils are considered under Muslim control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'tanfil' in Hanafi legal terminology?
A) Giving a fighter his regular share of spoils.
B) Giving a horseman extra beyond his regular share.
C) Distributing the salab (belongings of the killed).
D) Taking spoils before ihraz.

Key Takeaway
After spoils are secured, extra grants (nafal) can only come from the khums, and conditional promises must be interpreted strictly, with the default that the fighter gets only what is explicitly promised.

Nafal After Ihraz: Hanafi Position and Dispute with Ahl al-Sham
Inter-madhhab dispute on nafal after ihraz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on nafal after ihraz, explain the proof, and identify the dispute with Ahl al-Sham.

Core Idea
Nafal after ihraz from the soldiers' share is haram; only from khums is permissible.

This lesson examines the permissibility of granting additional rewards (nafal) from war spoils after they have been secured (ihraz). The Hanafi school strictly limits such grants to the one-fifth share (khums) to protect the soldiers' established rights, differing from Ahl al-Sham who permit nafal from the entire spoils. The passage also touches on internal Hanafi debates regarding giving nafal to the wealthy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school permits and prohibits regarding nafal after ihraz. Note the distinction between the four-fifths (soldiers' share) and the khums.
Abu Hanifa's statement: 'La nafal ba'da ihraz al-ghanimah.'
2
Identify the opposing school
Recognize that Ahl al-Sham (likely the Shafi'i school) permit nafal after ihraz without restriction.
Their exact proof is not given, but the Hanafi response addresses it.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the reasoning: nafal is for encouragement (tahrid), which is unnecessary after victory. Giving nafal would annul the soldiers' vested rights in the four-fifths.
Any historical instances of nafal after ihraz are explained as coming from the khums.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to Ahl al-Sham
The Hanafi response is that the very purpose of nafal is absent after ihraz, and the rights of soldiers are confirmed. Instances of nafal after ihraz were from the khums, not the four-fifths.
The text also addresses the terminology: 'la yanbaghi' implies prohibition.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi judge will only permit nafal from the khums after ihraz, while a Shafi'i judge may permit it from any portion.
This affects the distribution of spoils and the rights of soldiers.

His statement: (And he may grant nafal after ihraz from the khums only) because the right of others is confirmed by ihraz, and the soldiers have no right in the khums; what is given from the expenditures is for it; and giving nafal from it is only by virtue of spending on one of the three categories. Hence al-Dhakhira said: It is not fitting for the Imam to put it in the hands of the rich and make it nafal for him after the attainment because the khums is a right of the needy, not the rich; thus giving it to the rich invalidates their right. But their explicit statement that it is (called) tanfil indicates it is permissible for the rich. And surprisingly, al-Zayla'i said it is not permissible for the rich. If he does so and kills, he gets his salab, just as if he killed him in the ranks or after the rout. As for if he said that after they had drawn up for battle, it is (taken) as a remembrance of the battle until it ends, even if it lasts for days. The statement of the author: (And he grants nafal after ihraz from the khums...) in al-Manba' from al-Dhakhira: There is no disagreement among the scholars that tanfil before attainment and acquisition of spoils and before the war lays down its burdens is permissible. On the day of rout and the day of victory it is not permissible because the intent is encouragement to fight, and there is no need for it when the enemy is defeated and the Muslims prevail, for they do not fall short at that time but rather exert themselves without encouragement, so it involves annulling the rights of the soldiers and the poor without benefit. Hence it is not fitting (to give nafal) before victory and rout without exception; rather one should restrict (the offer): Whoever kills a killed one before the victory and rout gets his salab. If left absolute, it remains in those (cases). Do you not see that most of the killed and prisoners on the day of Badr were after the rout, and they were handed over to their capturers. As for after ihraz, it is not permissible except from the khums if (the recipient) is needy, because it is the right of the needy; and it is not fitting to place it among the needy. And the meaning of ihraz is that the spoils fall into the hands of the army and the detachment, summarized. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi, but what is in al-Zayla'i and others is the interpretation of ihraz as Dar al-Islam, which entails the permissibility of tanfil before the khums on the day of victory and rout, unless it is said that it is not a valid understanding according to the evidence that passed. And in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, Abu Hanifa said: There is no nafal after the acquisition of spoils, while the people of Syria (Ahl al-Sham) permit it after ihraz. What we have said is evidence of their error because nafal is for encouragement, and that is before attainment, not after; and because it establishes special entitlement initially, not to annul an established right of the soldiers, and giving nafal after attainment is annulling their right. Then he answered the objection that nafal after ihraz occurred (in the past) by saying it was from the khums. His statement: (Indeed, what appears in al-Dhakhira is that it is not prohibited—al-Nahr said: That is not correct; rather it clearly indicates prohibition, as the commentator said, because annulling the right of others is not permissible.) As for his using the expression 'not fitting' (la yanbaghi), it does not imply non-prohibition because it is not consistent (as a legal term); rather, what is omitted is more appropriate. Do you not see the statement in al-Hidayah: 'And it is fitting for the Muslims not to betray' and so on.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by commenting on the matn that nafal after ihraz is only from the khums. The reason is that after ihraz, the rights of the soldiers in the spoils are confirmed, and they have no right in the khums. The khums is for the needy categories mentioned in the Quran. Therefore, giving nafal from the khums is like spending on one of those categories. However, the text notes a difference among Hanafi scholars: al-Dhakhira says it is not fitting to give it to a rich person, but others argue the very term 'tanfil' implies it is permissible even for a rich person, since nafal is a form of grant. Al-Zayla'i's position that it is not permissible for the rich is considered strange. The passage then quotes from al-Manba' that all scholars agree nafal before the spoils are taken and before the war ends is permissible. However, on the day of victory or rout, it is not permissible because encouragement is unnecessary; giving nafal then would unjustly deprive the soldiers and the poor. Therefore, the Imam should restrict the offer to before victory. It then cites Abu Hanifa's statement that there is no nafal after ihraz, and notes that Ahl al-Sham (the Syrians, likely referring to the Shafi'i school) permit it after ihraz. The Hanafi proof is that nafal is for encouragement, which is not needed after the enemy is defeated, and it would annul the soldiers' established rights. Any instances of nafal after ihraz are explained as having come from the khums. The passage ends with a discussion of the term 'la yanbaghi' (it is not fitting) and whether it implies prohibition; the commentator argues it does, because annulling others' rights is haram.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Taking possession and securing the spoils; the context here defines it as the spoils falling into the hands of the army and detachment (others define it as reaching Dar al-Islam).
خمس (khums): The one-fifth share of the spoils that is set aside for the categories mentioned in Quran 8:41 (Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, wayfarers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, from which portion of the spoils may nafal be given after ihraz?
A) From the four-fifths soldiers' share.
B) From the khums only.
C) It is not permissible at all.
D) From any portion with the soldiers' consent.

Key Takeaway
Nafal after ihraz is restricted to the khums because it would otherwise annul the soldiers' established rights in the spoils.

Seizure and Ownership in Dar al-Harb: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tanfil
Defines ownership by disbelievers of each other's property in dar al-harb and Muslim acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi ruling on ownership by seizure in dar al-harb, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on tanfil.

Core Idea
In dar al-harb, seizure confers ownership, but full rights require ihraz – a condition disputed for bonus grants.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on property seizure among warring disbelievers in dar al-harb and subsequent acquisition by Muslims. The core principle is that property in dar al-harb is considered legally ownerless (mubah), so seizure by any party vests ownership. However, when Muslims acquire such property, a further condition of ihraz (bringing to Muslim territory) is required for full ownership rights. A notable internal dispute arises when the commander grants a bonus (tanfil) for a specific capture – does ownership vest immediately or only after ihraz? Understanding this difference is critical for proper application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of property in dar al-harb
The text establishes that property in dar al-harb is mubah (ownerless) for the purpose of seizure. This is the foundational premise: both the original owners and the captors are in dar al-harb, so seizure is a direct cause of ownership, analogous to gathering firewood.
This applies only when there is no treaty or protected status.
2
Define the ruling for Muslim acquisition
When Muslims overcome the victorious party and obtain the captured property, they own it because the property has left the ownership of the original non-Muslim owners. The ruling is unconditional regarding the existence of a truce, but qualified by the need for ihraz.
Ihraz is bringing the spoils to dar al-Islam.
3
Recognize the exception for fighting in Muslim territory with truce
If both warring groups have a truce with Muslims and they fight in Muslim territory, Muslims cannot buy from the victor because the property is still owned by the original owner (due to lack of ihraz). This would be treachery.
Betrayal of the treaty is prohibited.
4
Understand the dispute over tanfil (bonus grant)
When a commander grants a bonus for capturing a specific item (e.g., a slave girl), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that ownership does not occur until ihraz, while Muhammad holds that tanfil itself immediately vests ownership.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the majority view, the soldier cannot use or sell the captive until after ihraz.
5
Apply the proof for each position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf base their view on the general principle that ownership of spoils requires ihraz. Muhammad analogizes tanfil to division in dar al-harb or purchase from a harbi, which give immediate ownership.
The text does not provide a definitive tarjih; later Hanafi works may prefer the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب استيلاء الكفار
الملك سبب شامل لشيئين: استيلاء بعضهم على بعض واستيلائهم على أموالنا فقدم الأول. قوله: (سبى الترك الروم وأخذوا أموالهم ملكوها) لأن الاستيلاء قد تحقق في مال مباح وهو السبب لأن الكلام فيما إذا كان الكل في دار الحرب لأن الكافر يملك بمباشرة كالاحتطاب فكذا بهذا السبب. وفي القاموس: الروم بالضم جيل من ولد الروم بن عيصو، رجل رومي والجمع روم، والترك بالضم جيل من الناس والجمع أتراك. فما في النهاية من أن الترك جمع التركي والروم جمع الرومي ففيه نظر لا يخفى. قوله: (وملكنا ما نجده من ذلك إن غلبنا عليهم) اعتباراً بسائر أملاكهم. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بيننا وبين الروم موادعة لأنا لم نغدرهم إنما أخذنا ما لا خرج عن ملكهم ولذا حل لنا أن نشتري ما غنمه إحدى الطائفتين من الأخرى لما ذكرنا. وفي الخلاصة: الإحراز بدار الحرب شرط أما بدارهم فلا. ولو كان بيننا وبين كل من الطائفتين موادعة واقتتلوا في دارنا لا نشتري من الغالبين شيئاً لأنهم لم يملكوه لعدم الإحراز فيكون شراؤنا غدراً بالآخرين فإنه على ملكهم. وأما لو اقتتلت طائفتان في بلدة واحدة فهل يجوز شراء المسلم المستأمن من الغالبين؟ قال في فتح القدير: إن كان بين المأخوذ والآخذ قرابة محرمية كالأمية أو كان المأخوذ لا يجوز بيعه للآخذ لم يجز إلا إن دانوا بذلك عند الكرخي، وإن لم يكن فإن دانوا بأن من قهر آخر ملکه جاز الشراء وإلا فلا. قال آخراً: لو كان راكباً على بغل ونحوه لا يكون له ولو كان التنفيل بلفظ السلب لاستحقه لأن المركب أعم منه ومن الفرس. قال في القاموس: المركب كمقعد واحد مراكب البر والبحر. وفي الهداية: ثم حكم التنفيل قطع حق الباقين فأما الملك فإنما يثبت بعد الإحراز بدار الإسلام لما مر من قبل حتى لو قال الأمير من أصاب جارية فهي له فأصابها مسلم فاستبرأها لم يجز له وطؤها وكذا لا يبيعها هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد له أن يطاها ويبيعها لأن التنفيل يثبت به الملك عنده كما يثبت بالقسمة في دار الحرب والشراء من الحربي ووجوب الضمان بالإتلاف قد قيل على هذا الاختلاف. والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Chapter: Seizure by Disbelievers. The ownership cause includes two things: seizure of some by others and their seizure of our wealth. He presented the first. His statement: 'If the Turks capture the Romans and take their wealth, they own it' because seizure has occurred upon permissible (mubah) wealth, and that is the cause, because the speech is when all are in dar al-harb, for the disbeliever acquires ownership by direct action like gathering firewood, so also by this cause. In al-Qamus: ar-Rum (with damm) is a people from the descendants of Rum bin ‘Isa, and the plural is Rum; at-Turk (with damm) is a people and the plural is Atrak. So what is in an-Nihayah that Turk is plural of Turki and Rum plural of Rumi is not hidden. His statement: 'And we own what we find of that if we overcome them' as a consideration of the rest of their properties. He made it absolute, so it includes when there is a truce between us and the Romans, for we did not betray them; we only took what left their ownership. Hence it is permissible for us to buy what one of the two groups captured from the other for what we mentioned. In al-Khulasa: ihraz (taking possession) in dar al-harb is a condition, but in their own land it is not. If there is a truce between us and each of the two groups and they fight in our land, we do not buy anything from the victor because they did not own it due to lack of ihraz, so our purchase would be betrayal of the others as it is still their property. As for if two groups fight in one town, is it permissible for a Muslim who is musta'min to buy from the victor? In Fath al-Qadir: If there is a mahram relationship between the captured and the capturer, like being a mother, or if the captured cannot be sold to the capturer, it is not permissible unless they rule by that according to al-Karkhi. Otherwise, if they rule that whoever overcomes another owns him, then purchase is permissible; otherwise not. He further said: If he was riding a mule or similar, he does not get it; if the tanfil (bonus) was with the wording of salb (spoil), he would deserve it because the mount is more general than the horse. In al-Qamus: al-markab (mount) like masjid, one of the mounts of land and sea. In al-Hidayah: The ruling of tanfil is to cut off the right of the rest, but ownership is only established after ihraz in dar al-Islam as previously, so if the commander says whoever captures a slave girl gets her, and a Muslim captures her and performs istibra', he may not have intercourse with her nor sell her according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said he may have intercourse and sell because tanfil establishes ownership in his view, as established by division in dar al-harb and purchase from a harbi. The obligation of compensation by destruction has been said based on this difference. And Allah is Most High and Knows Best.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from the Kitab al-Siyar deals with the legal effect of seizure of property between warring non-Muslim groups (here Turks and Romans) in dar al-harb, and subsequent acquisition by Muslims. The ruling is that when one group of harbis captures another's property in dar al-harb, they own it because the property was originally mubah (ownerless from a legal perspective) and seizure in dar al-harb causes ownership. This is analogous to a disbeliever acquiring raw materials by direct action like gathering firewood. When Muslims later seize that same property from the harbis upon defeating them, Muslims also own it, as the property has left the ownership of the original non-Muslim owners. The rule is unconditional but qualified by the need for ihraz (actual possession and removal to Muslim-controlled territory) for the ownership to be complete. The text discusses exceptions when there is a treaty (muwada‘a) between Muslims and the warring groups: if the fighting occurs in Muslim territory, Muslims cannot purchase from the victor because the property is still under the original owner's ownership, and buying from the victor would be treachery. There is also a ruling about a specific scenario where the commander gives a bonus (tanfil) to a soldier for capturing a specific item. A dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Muhammad on the other is reported: the former hold that ownership is not established until the spoils are brought to dar al-Islam, so the soldier may not use or sell the captive; Muhammad holds that tanfil itself establishes ownership immediately, so he may. The relied-upon position is not specified here.

Key Terms
استيلاء (istila'): Seizure or taking possession, especially in war context in dar al-harb.
إحراز (ihraz): Taking possession and bringing to safety (e.g., to Muslim territory) to complete ownership.
تنفيل (tanfil): A bonus grant by the commander to a soldier for capturing specific spoils.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not enforced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute over tanfil, what is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding a soldier's right to have intercourse with a captured slave girl before the spoils are brought to dar al-Islam?
A) The soldier may have intercourse immediately because tanfil grants ownership.
B) The soldier may not have intercourse or sell her until the spoils are ihraz'ed to dar al-Islam.
C) The soldier may only sell her but not have intercourse.
D) The soldier may have intercourse but cannot sell her.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, seizure in dar al-harb is a cause of ownership, but full rights of disposition depend on the condition of ihraz, except in the view of Muhammad who holds that a commander's bonus grants immediate ownership.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Enemy Ownership of Muslim Property in Dar al-Harb
Inter-madhhab dispute on whether enemy owns Muslim property brought into their territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on enemy ownership of Muslim property brought into dar al-harb and explain why the Hanafi school differs from Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The enemy owns captured property because loss of benefit lifts immunity, not because seizure is permissible.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a sharp legal disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. At issue is whether the enemy gains rightful ownership over Muslim property they capture and bring into their own territory. The Hanafi ruling rests on a subtle distinction between inherent prohibition and prohibition due to an external factor.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: that the enemy owns Muslim property they seize and bring into dar al-harb (ihraz).
The text states 'ملكوها' (they own it).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that the enemy does not own such property because the seizure is prohibited in itself.
Shafi'i argues that a prohibited act cannot be a cause for ownership.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: seizure is prohibited from beginning to end, and what is prohibited cannot serve as a cause for ownership.
This is based on a general principle that prohibited acts yield no legal ownership.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts this: the prohibition is for something else (mahzur li-ghayrihi), not inherent; the property reverts to being permissible because the original owner can no longer benefit from it.
The Hanafis cite the Quranic verse 'He created for you all that is in the earth' to show original permissibility, which is only lifted for the owner's benefit; when benefit is lost, the property returns to mubah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Ascertain the practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the enemy can sell or use the property; under Shafi'i, the property remains with the original owner if recovered.
This affects recovery obligations and treatment of captors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب استيلاء الكفار عليهم وإن غلبوا على أموالنا وأحرزوها بدارهم ملكوها وقال الشافعي لا يملكونها لأن الاستيلاء محظور ابتداء وانتهاء والمحظور لا ينتهض سبباً للملك على ما عرف من قاعدة الخصم ولنا أن الاستيلاء ورد على مال مباح فنيعقد سبباً للملك دفعاً لحاجة المكلف كاستيلائنا على مالهم، وهذا لأن العصمة ثبتت على منافاة الدليل ضرورة تمكن المالك من الانتفاع، وإذا زالت المكنة عاد مباحاً كما كان غير أن الاستيلاء لا يتحقق إلا بالإحراز بالدار لأنه عبارة عن الاقتدار على المحل حالاً ومآلاً، والمحظور لغيره إذا صلح سبباً لكرامة تفوق الملك وهو الثواب الآجل فما ظنك بالملك العاجل؟ قيد بالإحراز لأنهم لو استولوا عليها فظهرنا عليهم قبل الإحراز فإنها تكون لملاكها بغير شيء، ولو اقتسموها في دارنا لم يملكوا. وفي المحيط يفرض علينا اتباعهم ومقاتلتهم لاستنقاذ الأموال من أيديهم ما داموا في دار الإسلام، وإن دخولوا بها دار الحرب لا يفترض علينا اتباعهم. والأولى اتباعهم بخلاف الذراري يفترض اتباعهم مطلقاً. وأفاد المصنف رحمه الله أنهم لو أسلموا فلا سبيل لأربابها عليها؛ كذا في شرح الطحاوي.
The chapter of siyar / section on the enemy overpowering them. And if they overcome our property and bring it into their territory, they own it. Al-Shafi'i said: They do not own it because seizure is prohibited in its beginning and end, and what is prohibited cannot be a cause for ownership according to the opponent's principle. Our evidence: The seizure occurred on permissible property, so it becomes a cause for ownership to fulfill the need of the obligated person, like our seizure of their property. This is because immunity (isma) is established contrary to the evidence (the verse 'He created for you all that is in the earth') out of necessity for the owner to benefit. When the ability to benefit is removed, it reverts to being permissible as it was. However, seizure is not realized except by bringing it into their territory because it means power over the property now and in the future. And what is prohibited for something else can be a cause for a honor greater than ownership, namely future reward, so what do you think of immediate ownership? He restricted with 'bringing it into their territory' because if they seized it but we defeated them before they brought it into their territory, it remains for its owners without compensation. And if they divided it in our territory, they do not own it. In al-Muhit: It is obligatory for us to pursue and fight them to recover property as long as they are in dar al-Islam; if they enter dar al-harb, it is not obligatory to pursue them. The preferable view is to pursue them, unlike children for whom pursuit is obligatory unconditionally. The author (rahimahullah) stated that if they become Muslim, the original owners have no claim to it; as in Sharh al-Tahawi.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether the enemy owns Muslim property they capture and bring into their territory (dar al-harb). The Hanafi position is that they do own it. The author begins by stating the matn ruling: 'If they overcome our property and bring it into their territory, they own it.' Then he presents the Shafi'i objection: seizure is prohibited in itself and cannot be a cause for ownership. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition is not inherent; the 'illa is that the property becomes permissible because the original owner can no longer benefit from it. The author supports this by referencing the Quranic verse 'He created for you all that is in the earth,' which makes property permissible. Overriding this verse required the owner's ability to benefit; when that ability is lost, the property reverts to being permissible. The enemy's seizure is not complete unless the property is brought into their territory (ihraz). Before that, if Muslims recover it, the original owner gets it free. The author also clarifies that if the enemy becomes Muslim, the original owners have no claim.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Bringing property into the enemy's territory (dar al-harb), making it subject to their control.
عصمة (isma): Protection of property rights that prevents others from taking it; here, it is conditional on the owner's ability to benefit.
محظور لغيره (mahzur li-ghayrihi): An act prohibited not in itself but due to an external factor; can still be a cause for ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of Muslim property taken by the enemy and brought into dar al-harb?
A) It remains owned by the original Muslim owner.
B) The enemy owns it.
C) It becomes ownerless (mubah).
D) It belongs to the Muslim state.

Key Takeaway
The enemy owns captured Muslim property brought into dar al-harb because the original owner's inability to benefit removes the property's immunity, and the prohibition on seizure does not prevent it from being a cause for ownership.

Recovering Property from Spoils: Before and After Division
Ruling with Hadith proof and legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for recovering one's property from the enemy before and after division, and explain the rationale based on the hadith and the principle of balancing harm.

Core Idea
Property found before division is taken free; after division, it is taken with compensation to balance harm.

This lesson examines a key ruling in the Hanafi fiqh of jihad: what happens when a Muslim finds his own property among the spoils of war? The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a clear distinction based on timing—before or after division—and supports it with a prophetic hadith. We will analyze the legal reasoning behind this distinction and its implications for different types of property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: 'Whoever finds his property before division takes it for free; after division, with price.' Note the two scenarios.
2
Examine the dalil
The hadith is quoted. Identify the operative phrase that distinguishes the two rulings.
The hadith is the primary evidence.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The commentary explains: before division, harm is minimal due to common ownership; after division, the owner must pay to avoid harming the current possessor.
This is an application of the principle of balancing interests.
4
Distinguish between property types
Note the author's indication that this ruling applies to qimi (unique) property; for mithli (fungible) like money, after division the owner cannot reclaim because taking a like gives no benefit.
This is a crucial qualification.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: a Muslim finds his camel (qimi) among spoils already divided. What must he do? State the ruling and justification.
Use the hadith and reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن غلبنا عليهم فمن وجد ملكه قبل القسمة أخذه مجاناً وبعدها بالقيمة) لقوله عليه السلام فيه : إن وجدته قبل القسمة فهو لك بغير شيء، وإن وجدته بعد القسمة فهو لك بالقيمة. ولأن المالك القديم زال ملكه بغير رضاه فكان له حق الأخذ نظراً له إلا أن في الأخذ بعد القسمة ضرراً بالمأخوذ منه بإزالة ملكه الخاص فيأخذه بالقيمة ليعتدل النظر من الجانبين، والشركة قبل القسمة عامة فيقل الضرر فيأخذه بغير قيمته أطلقه فشمل ما إذا ترك أخذه بعد العلم به زماناً طويلاً بعد الإخراج من دار الحرب كما سيأتي. وأشار بقوله «بقيمته» إلى أن الكلام في القيمي لأن النقدين والمكيل والموزون لا سبيل له عليه بعد القسمة لأنه لو أخذه أخذه بمثله وذلك لا يفيد وقبيل القسمة يأخذه مجاناً؛ كذا المحيط :
His statement (the author's): (And if we overpower them, then whoever finds his property before division takes it for free, and after division takes it with price) for his statement (peace be upon him) concerning it: 'If you find it before division, it is yours without anything; if you find it after division, it is yours with price.' And because the original owner's ownership was removed without his consent, so he has the right to take it as a consideration for him, except that taking it after division causes harm to the one from whom it is taken by removing his specific ownership, so he takes it with price to balance consideration from both sides. And common ownership before division is general, so harm is less, so he takes it without its price. He gave it absolutely, so it includes if he delayed taking it after knowing about it for a long time after removal from dar al-harb, as will come. And he indicated by his word 'with its price' that it concerns fungible property (qimi), because dirham and dinar and measurable or weighable goods: the owner has no claim on them after division, because if he took them, he would take them by their like, and that gives no benefit. And before division, he takes them for free. As in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for when Muslims recover property from the enemy. The matn says: whoever finds his own property before the division of spoils takes it free; if after division, he takes it by paying its price (value). The evidence is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The reasoning: the original owner lost his property without consent, so he has a right to reclaim it. But after division, the spoils have been divided among the Muslims, so taking it without compensation would harm the current possessor. Therefore, the owner must pay the price to balance interests. Before division, the property is still in common ownership, so harm is minimal, and he takes it free. The author notes that this applies to items that have a unique value (qimi); for fungible goods like money or measures, the owner cannot reclaim after division because he would only get a like item (misl), which is no advantage. Before division, however, he takes such goods free. This ruling covers even if the owner delays claiming for a long time.

Key Terms
قيمي (qimi): Property that has a unique value and cannot be replaced exactly by its like (e.g., a specific animal or land).
مثلي (mithli): Fungible goods that have standardized measures (e.g., dirhams, wheat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim finds his own property among spoils that have already been divided, what must he do to reclaim it?
A) Take it for free.
B) Pay the price (value) to the current possessor.
C) He cannot reclaim it at all.
D) He must return it to the state.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between recovering property before division (free) and after division (with price) based on a prophetic hadith and the principle of balancing harm.

Recovering a Captured Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on reclaiming a slave captured and freed by enemy, later recovered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recovery of a captured slave who escapes with enemy property, identify the conditions that affect the ruling, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The master of a captured slave may reclaim him free only if he arrives before the imam extracts the one-fifth; otherwise he must pay.

When a Muslim slave is captured by the enemy, then escapes with enemy property to dar al-Islam and is seized by another Muslim, who owns the slave? The Hanafi school has an internal debate between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, with Muhammad eventually retracting his initial view. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence for the master.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the facts: a captured slave escapes from enemy territory, takes enemy property, and enters dar al-Islam where a Muslim seizes him. The master then appears.
This is a composite scenario from the texts.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave becomes fay' (community property) upon entering dar al-Islam. Therefore the master may take him free, and the captor has no claim. The property the slave took is also fay'.
Fay' belongs to the public treasury; the imam distributes it.
3
Present Muhammad al-Shaybani's initial view and retraction
Muhammad initially ruled that the captor owns the slave as ghanimah (spoils), so the master must pay a price. Later he retracted, distinguishing whether the master arrives before or after the imam takes one-fifth (khums). If before, the master takes free; if after, he pays.
Muhammad's retraction reflects a shift from ghanimah analogy to a middle position.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
According to al-TatarKhaniyya, Muhammad's final view is the relied-upon position. The master's right is conditioned on timing relative to khums extraction.
The legal effect: the captor retains four-fifths of the slave's value if the master comes late.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : عبد المسلم سباه أهل الحرب فأعتقه سيده ثم غلب عليه المسلمون أخذه مولاه بغير شيء وذلك العتق باطل، ولو أعتقه بعد ما أخرجه المسلمون قبل القسمة جاز عتقه . عبد المسلم الذي هو جمع تركي جمع على أتراك وهذا لا ينفيه صاحب النهاية . أسره العدوّ وأحرز بدارهم ثم انفلت منهم وأخذ شيئاً من أموالهم وخرج هارباً إلى دار الإسلام فأخذه مسلم ثم جاء مولاه لم يأخذه منه إلا بالقيمة في قول محمد، وما في يده من المال فهو لمن أخذه ولا سبيل للمولى عليه وأما في قياس قول أبي حنيفة فإن المولى يأخذ العبد بغير شيء لأنه لما دخل دار الإسلام صار فيئاً لجماعة المسلمين يأخذه الإمام ويرفع خمسه ويقسم أربعة أخماسه بين الغانمين، ثم رجع محمد عن قوله وقال : إذا أخذه مسلم فهو غنيمة آخذه وأخمسه إذا لم يحضر المولى واجعل أربعة أخماس العبد والمال الذي معه للآخذ، فإن جاء مولاه بعد ذلك أخذه بالقيمة، وإن جاء مولاه قبل أن يخمس أخذه بغير شيء اهـ. وفي الملتقط : عبد أسره أهل الحرب والحقوه بدارهم ثم أبق منهم يرد إلى سيده وفي رواية يعتق اهـ.
And in al-TatarKhaniyya: A Muslim slave was captured by the people of war (enemy) and his master freed him, then the Muslims overcame (the enemy). His master takes him without anything, and that emancipation is void. If he freed him after the Muslims brought him out, before division, his emancipation is valid. [Note on etymology: 'Abd al-Muslim' is a plural of Turkish origin, etc.] The enemy captured him and brought him into their territory, then he escaped from them and took some of their property and fled to dar al-Islam. A Muslim seized him, then his master came; he does not take him from the Muslim except with price, according to the saying of Muhammad. And what is in his hand of property belongs to the one who seized him, and the master has no claim on it. In the analogy of Abu Hanifa's saying, the master takes the slave without anything, because when he entered dar al-Islam, he became fay' for the community of Muslims; the imam takes him and takes out one-fifth and divides the remaining four-fifths among the warriors. Then Muhammad retracted his saying and said: If a Muslim seized him, it is ghanimah: I take it and extract one-fifth if the master is not present, and I make four-fifths of the slave and the property with him for the taker. Then if his master comes after that, he takes him with price. If his master comes before he extracts the one-fifth, he takes him without anything. End. And in al-Multaqat: A slave was captured by the enemy and they brought him into their territory, then he fled from them, he is returned to his master; and in one narration, he is freed.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific scenario: a Muslim slave captured by the enemy, then freed by his master while still in enemy hands, then the Muslims defeat the enemy and recover the slave. According to the text, the master takes the slave free, and the freeing is void (because the slave was still in enemy possession and the master's ownership had not ended? The reasoning is that the enemy's ownership replaces the master's). Then a more complex scenario: the slave escapes from the enemy, takes some of their property, and flees to dar al-Islam. Another Muslim captures him. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the original master can only take him by paying a price (value) to the Muslim who captured him. The property the slave took belongs to the captor. According to the analogy (qiyas) of Abu Hanifa's school, the master takes the slave free, because when the slave entered dar al-Islam, he becomes fay' (booty for the community) and goes through the imam's distribution. However, Muhammad later retracted and said if a Muslim individual seized him, it is ghanimah (spoils proper), so the imam takes one-fifth and gives four-fifths to the captor. If the master comes after that, he pays price; if he comes before the one-fifth is taken, he takes free. Finally, a narration from al-Multaqat: if a slave flees the enemy, he returns to his master or is freed.

Key Terms
فَيْء (fay'): Property taken from enemy without warfare; here used for a slave who enters dar al-Islam after escape.
غَنِيمَة (ghanimah): Spoils taken through warfare; here refers to property taken from enemy by a Muslim individual.
خُمْس (khums): One-fifth share of ghanimah that goes to the imam for public treasury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani's final ruling, when does the master of a captured slave take the slave free?
A) Always, regardless of timing.
B) If he comes after the Muslim captures the slave.
C) If he comes before the imam extracts one-fifth (khums).
D) Never; he must always pay.

Key Takeaway
The master's right to reclaim his captured slave is conditional: free if before khums, with payment if after, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position.
